 title : The net-bittorrent Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Net_GearmanAboutNet_Gearman is a PEAR package for interfacing with Danga&#39;s Gearman. Gearman is a system to farm out work to other machines, dispatching function calls to machines that are better suited to do work, to do work in parallel, to load balance lots of function calls, or to call functions between languages. </p>

<p>Net_Gearman is currently in production at Yahoo! and Digg doing all sorts of offloaded near time processing. </p>

<p>InstallationInstall PEAR if it is not already installed on your system. Run pear install http://netgearman.googlecode.com/files/Net_Gearman-x.y.z.tgz (Replace x.y.z with the latest version from the featured download to the right).  ExamplesClient&lt;?php</p>

<p>require_once &#39;Net/Gearman/Client.php&#39;;</p>

<p>$client = new Net_Gearman_Client(&#39;localhost:7003&#39;);
<br/>$client-&gt;someBackgroundJob(array(
<br/>    &#39;userid&#39; =&gt; 5555,
<br/>    &#39;action&#39; =&gt; &#39;new-comment&#39;
<br/>));</p>

<p>?&gt;Job&lt;?php</p>

<p>class Net_Gearman_Job_someBackgroundJob extends Net_Gearman_Job_Common
<br/>{
<br/>    public function run($args)
<br/>    {
<br/>        if (!isset($args[&#39;userid&#39;]) || !isset($args[&#39;action&#39;])) {
<br/>            throw new Net_Gearman_Job_Exception(&#39;Invalid/Missing arguments&#39;);
<br/>        }</p>

<p>        // Insert a record or something based on the $args</p>

<p>        return array(); // Results are returned to Gearman, except for 
<br/>                        // background jobs like this one.
<br/>    }
<br/>}</p>

<p>?&gt;Worker&lt;?php</p>

<p>require_once &#39;Net/Gearman/Worker.php&#39;;</p>

<p>$worker = new Net_Gearman_Worker(&#39;localhost:7003&#39;);
<br/>$worker-&gt;addAbility(&#39;someBackgroundJob&#39;);
<br/>$worker-&gt;beginWork();</p>

<p>?&gt;</p>
 title : The netgearman Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is a wrapper library around the Mollom API. The library is written in C#, and uses the excellent XmlRpc library created by Charles Cook. </p>

<p>At the moment this is just a library wrapper around the API, abstracting the XmlRpc calls away. The objects returned by the library are serializable, so they can be stored in the ViewState or the Session objects. This is necessary to facilitate the Mollom session management, which is almost completely abstracted away.  </p>

<p>GettingThe latest version is NMollom 1.0.2.0, which targets Mollom/1.0. </p>

<p>You can download nmollom as a binary package: nmollom-1.0.2.0.zip. This includes the nmollom dll and the xmlrpc dll. </p>

<p>Alternatively, get the source from the svn repository and build it yourself. </p>

<p>ExamplesSee the MollomTestSite in the svn repository for an example on how to use the library.  You&#39;ll need to rename/copy example-web.config in the site&#39;s root, and fill in your own keys there to try it out. The site assumes that the keys used are in &quot;development mode&quot; at mollom (see their documentation on more info on &quot;development mode&quot;). </p>

<p>You can apply for a set of public-private keys at the Mollom site. </p>

<p>VersioningThe major and minor version of the NMollom assembly will always reflect the version of the Mollom API it is targeting. So version 1.0.2.0 targets Mollom/1.0.</p>

 title : The obremsdk Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ObremSDKcirca April 2007 by Neil C. Obremski </p>

<p>Welcome. </p>

<p>Someday I&#39;ll write something meaningful here, but until then just go play with my source. </p>

<p>C# .NET ConventionsTired of DLL and Assembly hell?  Try static linking instead with ObremSDK classes: a daily dose of code gems will keep your application healthy and fit.  Copy individual obrem-.cs files into your project tree or share the ObremSDK sub-folder of your choice using the svn:externals property in your project&#39;s Subversion repository. </p>

<p>Functionality isolated using classes not namespaces. Class source files prefixed with &quot;obrem-&quot;. Class names are preceded by &quot;Obrem&quot;. Classes of the same name between different versions (dotnet vs dotnet20 do the same thing; this goes for their members as well. Most .NET functions are static. The .NET version-specific folders are used only when the implementation of a class must differ between .NET versions.  An application must never include both of these, otherwise name conflicts will occur. The NET_20 macro will be checked for compiling .NET 2.0-optimized code in the general &quot;dotnet&quot; folder. Experimental functions and classes are suffixed with an underscore, i.e. SomeNewFoo. ASP.NET 2.0 RecommendationsAdd obremsdk/dotnet/ and obremsdk/dotnet20/ as svn:externals in your App_Code directory.</p>

 title : The xadp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The X AOLserver Dynamic Platform (xADP) is a &quot;batteries included&quot; distribution for AOLserver. It includes, but is not limited to, Tcl, AOLserver, MySQL, cURL, TclCurl, tDOM, Tcllib, nsrpc, and nsdb.  Using a single Makefile to build and link these features together, xADP offers an out-of-the-box experience for AOLserver.  xADP provides simple mechanisms for starting and stopping servers, server communication via RPC, and a nsdb Tcl package that wraps the ns_db API for ease of use.   </p>

<p>To install xADP, first check out the src from svn: </p>

<p>svn checkout http://xadp.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ xadp 
<br/>Then read the README file for installation instructions and documentation. </p>

<p>Note: xADP has only been tested on Darwin_i366. Please let me know if you have issues on other platforms.</p>

 title : The benchmark4j Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Java (and UNIX) has for a long time lacked the equivalent (for the most part) of Windows perfmon. While perfmon was by no means perfect the goals were admirable. Developers could export simple statistics from their application and perfmon could introspect the values and graph them. </p>

 title : The bigcache Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>OverviewBigCache is a very simple cache API providing users with an infinite shared cache backed by Amazon S3. No servers required. </p>

<p>Here&#39;s a quick code sample for how to use it. </p>

<p>// put an object into the cache
<br/>bigcache.put(&quot;somekey&quot;, myObject, 3600);</p>

<p>// Get an object from the cache
<br/>Object o = bigcache.get(&quot;somekey&quot;);News2008-11-14 Added asynchronous methods getAsync(key) and putAsync(key, object, expires) </p>

<p>BackgroundWhile testing out different caching scenarios, I got the idea of using S3 as a simple cache like memcached and decided to run some tests.  This is what typical test times look like running on an EC2 server (the memcached was running on a separate server) for retrieving 100 simple strings: </p>

<p>Memcached took: 219 S3 took: 2679 SDB took: 2302 ehcache memory took: 1 ehcache 95% disk took: 11 Memcached mod took: 219 S3 mod took: 2203 UPDATE: New AsyncMethods need to be added to this benchmark, big performance gains when using them.  </p>

<p>The last two mod tests retrieved 100 times, but only 10 different objects to see if S3 did any caching on recently retrieved items.  Running this repeatedly revealed very similar results time after time. I realize this isn&#39;t exactly the greatest benchmarking test, so no need to let me know otherwise. ;)  </p>

<p>So what can we gather from this: </p>

<p>In Memory is ultra fast (of course) From local disk is also extremely fast (although much slower than in memory, 10x) Memcached is amazingly fast too, especially considering it&#39;s over the network, apparently 2 ms per object (although much slower than in memory or local disk, 20x vs disk) S3 and SimpleDB were similar when retreiving directly by key/id, but both were much slower than any other solution at about 25ms per object, 10x vs memcached) So now you might say, &quot;well obviously memcached is the way to go for large scale caching&quot;, and I would have to agree fully. BUT what about the extra work required to run a pool of extra servers just for memcached? When you&#39;ve already got a ready to go infinite cache available in S3.  </p>

<p>Double Layer CacheNow you could just use S3 if you could live with the slowness, but the following scenario is an alternative that gives you the ultra fast memory/disk combo for your local cache and the slower S3 as the global shared cache. And usually your local disk is pretty much unused anyways so this makes good use of it.  It is like a chained cache consisting of in memory and disk caching (ehcache) with S3 as a secondary cache.  For example: </p>

<p>getObject(key){
<br/>   object = localCache.get(key);
<br/>   if(object != null) return object;
<br/>   object = s3cache.get(key);
<br/>   if(object != null) {
<br/>     localCache.put(key, object);
<br/>     return object;
<br/>   }
<br/>   object = getFromDatabase(key);
<br/>   if(object != null){
<br/>     localCache.put(key, object);
<br/>     s3Cache.put(key, object);
<br/>     return object;
<br/>   }
<br/>   return null;
<br/>}This scenario would fully support stateless/sessionless load balancing although if you had a ton of app servers and your data was pretty user specific (private), then local/disk cache might become useless unless you have sticky sessions enabled on your load balancer. It would really depend on your app.   </p>

<p>Other Performance ComparisonsGreg Luck, the creator of EhCache, compares ehcache and memcached Kevin Burton retaliates against Greg&#39;s comparison</p>

 title : The cqxmlintf Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A TCP socket-based service layer on ClearQuest that enables platform-independent clients to execute ClearQuest commands via XML. </p>

<p>OverviewThe ClearQuest XML Interface is a service layer on IBM&#39;s ClearQuest that allows platform-independent clients to send ClearQuest commands via XML. IBM&#39;s comparable solution required additional server hardware and installation of proprietary software on each client machine. Additionally, our implementation works better over the WAN, is scalable and utilizes a generic interface. </p>

<p>DetailsThe ClearQuest XML Interface (CQ/XML) is a service that waits for incoming TCP socket connections. Upon a successful connection, CQ/XML reads the XML coming through the socket. If the XML is not well-formatted, CQ/XML sends an XML-formatted error back to the sender. If the XML is well-formatted, CQ/XML logs-in to ClearQuest as the connecting user. The parsed commands are then executed within ClearQuest as that user. The result from each command is saved, reformatted as XML and sent back through the socket to the client before closing the socket. </p>

<p>JustificationThe use of CQ/XML as a &quot;ClearQuest layer&quot; instead of a &quot;database layer&quot; gives us several advantages over the direct database access that some of our customers have asked for. For one, ClearQuest business rules are still enforced. Secondly, we can enforce ClearQuest logins and passwords. Most importantly, ClearQuest history is maintained without compromising the integrity of the database. </p>

<p>ResultsCQ/XML has been extremely stable, with no application-level failures encountered through seven months of testing and fifteen months of production deployment. It scales extremely well. Under Sun Grid Engine tests, CQ/XML was still handling requests with over 350 near-simultaneous connections. Our user community has created several amazing extensions to ClearQuest, including completely new web interfaces, GUI-enabled version control system integrations, RSS feeds, plus more. Time permitting, we&#39;d love to clean them up and post them out here as well.</p>

 title : The cuhofra Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Customizable Homepage FrameworkIntroductionThere are many different ways to set up a homepage. Which one you take is decided by your requirements. If you only want to present an amount of information which changes infrequently it is recommend to use a basically static way to create your homepage. In this case your website does not need to have lots of dynamic features and it is less necessary to have a modifiable structure. To build such a homepage there are lots of developement tools at the market. </p>

<p>But if you wish to start a more flexible and dynamic homepage project this possibilities are not applicable. To instantiate such a project you need certain programming techniques rarely handled by people which just want to set up a homepage project. </p>

<p>The goal of this project is to create a flexible structure of a homepage. The customer should be able to assemble the homepage of his desire from a pool of software parts. He gets a basic part including the most significant functions and interfaces to extend the functionality with different modules without being obliged to know the handling and background of the technologies used to realize such extensive projects. </p>

<p>News 2008-07-21 | Summarize the working time  </p>

<p>The assistant tool Create Statistics is now able read the working time TeX document and generate a summarizing document with the amount of hours of the given domains and subdomains. </p>

<p> 2008-07-18 | Assistant tool Create Statistics  </p>

<p>The developement of an assistang tool named Create Statistics has begun. This tool based on Python and wxPython should be able to generate a summary of the working time document. It will summarize the given domains and creates a new TeX document with the results. Furthermore the tool should create SVN graphics to visualize the amount of hours of the different domains. The code of the tool is located in /trunk/docs/project_management/working_time. </p>

<p> 2008-06-26 | Time tracking defined  </p>

<p>The modality how to record the time spended to this project is specified. There will be a LaTeX document in trunk/docs/project_management/working_time in which all working times will be recorded. Every work unit is dedicated to one of before specified domains and contains also the date, the amount of hours and a description of the activity. </p>

 title : The induslearningframework Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Indus Learning Framework(ILF)The indus learning framework is a suite of machine learning algorithms that learn from  datasets using sufficient statistics.  This framework is particularly useful in the following scenarios: </p>

<p> When the data set is huge and the it cannot be fit into memory (e.g arff file is huge and weka runs out of memory) </p>

<p> When access to underlying data instances is not available (due to considerations such as security or cost) but the datasources provides some statistics (like count queries) The current implementation of the framework provides Naive Bayes and Decison Trees. The framework has been written so that it can be extended to include more classifiers that are amenable to the sufficient statistics approach. </p>

<p>Refer the user&#39;s guide wiki for how to run the various classifiers in the framework. Besides being run from command line the ILF allows provides API which can be used to integrated into a target application. </p>

<p>Integration Samplessample 1import airldm2.core.datatypes.relational.SingleRelationDataDescriptor;
<br/>import airldm2.core.datatypes.relational.RelationalDataSource;
<br/>import  airldm2.util.SimpleArffFileReader;
<br/>import airldm2.classifiers.Evaluation
<br/>import weka.classifiers.evaluation.ConfusionMatrix;
<br/>import weka.core.Utils;</p>

<p>........
<br/>.......</p>

<p>String[] options= {&quot;-b&quot;,  &quot;-trainTable&quot;, &quot;votes_train&quot;, &quot;-testFile&quot;,&quot;sample/HouseVotesTrain.arff&quot;};
<br/>    
<br/>          
<br/>String trainTableName = Utils.getOption(&quot;trainTable&quot;, options);
<br/>String testFile = Utils.getOption(&quot;testFile&quot;, options);</p>

<p>NaiveBayesClassifier classifier = new NaiveBayesClassifier();
<br/>         
<br/>SingleRelationDataDescriptor  desc = null;
<br/>     
<br/>      
<br/>SimpleArffFileReader readTest = new SimpleArffFileReader(testFile);
<br/>LDTestInstances testInst = readTest.getTestInstances();
<br/>desc = (SingleRelationDataDescriptor )testInst.getDesc();
<br/>         
<br/>SSDataSource dataSource = new RelationalDataSource(trainTableName);
<br/>// Create a Large DataSet Instance and set its descriptor and source
<br/>LDInstances trainData = new LDInstances();
<br/>trainData.setDesc(desc);
<br/>trainData.setDataSource(dataSource);
<br/>         
<br/>ConfusionMatrix matrix = Evaluation.evlauateModel2(classifier, trainData, testInst, options);
<br/>System.out.println(matrix.toString(&quot;===Confusion Matrix===&quot;));
<br/>         </p>

<p>      Extension With Indus Integration FrameworkThe system can use a data integration system to be able to learn from multiple disparate data sources. The current implementation has been extended to use  Indus Integration Framework.  User&#39;s are referred to the code and an example included in the source tree induse_extension_src </p>

<p>For feature requests contact neeraj.kaul@gmail.com</p>

 title : The jgoogleanalytics Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>IntroductionJGoogleAnalytics is a lightweight, unobtrusive Java utility for tracking usage information on Java applications through Google analytics. It can be used for gathering usage statistics on utilities, plugins(Eclipse, IntelliJ, Netbeans etc.), client-side, server-side, middleware, desktop or any Java based applications. Hence, allowing us to perform usage &amp; trend analysis on the application of interest. </p>

<p>UsageIf you have a registered Google analytics account, you can write a code snippet like below to capture the usage data. FocusPoint is a logical point of focus in the application. It can be events like application/module load, user actions, error events etc. </p>

<p>  //Google analytics tracking code for Library Finder
<br/>  JGoogleAnalyticsTracker tracker = new JGoogleAnalyticsTracker(&quot;Library Finder&quot;,&quot;1.3.2&quot;,&quot;UA-2184000-1&quot;);</p>

<p>  FocusPoint focusPoint = new FocusPoint(&quot;PluginLoad&quot;);</p>

<p>  tracker.trackAsynchronously(focusPoint);Proof Of ConceptFor the proof of concept, I have used this tool in Library Finder-IntelliJ plugin. I was tracking events like plugin load, user actions like Find Library action, Configuration changes action etc. I could see the usage statistics when I login to the google analytics account. If you want to know more, please read this posting. </p>

<p>CaveatGoogle analytics does not update their reports in real time because of their high volume of subscribers. It usually gets updated every 24 hrs. If you are really curious to know if the tracking went fine, you can attach a LoggingAdapter to JGoogleAnalyticsTracker and see if you are seeing the success message. JGoogleAnalytics would gracefully ignore errors and not collect statistics for the application running offline (without network connectivity)</p>

 title : The jordens-jdbcspy Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>JDBCSpy </p>

<p>ObjectiveJDBCSpy aims to provide a lightweight means to obtain statistics at the JDBC driver level. </p>

<p>StatusIt currently provides minimal statistics around JDBC Statements and PreparedStatements but functionality is expected to improve over time. </p>

<p>JDBCSpy has been tested using PostgreSQL and hsqldb but should more or less work with any configurable JDBC data source. </p>

<p>The code is a work in progress (and likely will continue to be for the foreseeable future). It&#39;s an interesting little side project that has actually shown some utility in a couple of situations.  </p>

<p>DependenciesThere are no run-time dependencies.  JDBCSpy (jdbcspy-core) has test-time dependencies on TestNG and hsqldb. </p>

<p>See the installation instructions for information on getting started. </p>

<p>Future PlansSupport for more Statement/PreparedStatement methods (currently only tracks executeQuery()) Provide a nice UI for statistics visualization (Currently in development) Recent Commits03/14/08Significant refactors around the viewing components (there have been a few commits over the last few month that haven&#39;t been accurately recorded on the project page). </p>

<p>What: </p>

<p>Introduced a common interface between GUI panels and the QueryStatistics they&#39;re displaying. Replaying a session from a JDBCSpy logfile should now work a little better. </p>

<p>01/03/08The result of some work performed during my pre-Christmas hack day. </p>

<p>What: </p>

<p>Updated to Surefire 2.4 and TestNG 5.7 </p>

<p>Two new JDBCSpyMBean interface methods: mark() and getSQLExecutionTime(). mark() allows you to explicitly have a message logged getSQLExecutionTime() provides the number of milliseconds spent executing SQL since the last reset. Introduced new module: jdbcspy-testutil JDBCSpyListener provides framework hooks to track SQL execution during TestNG test cases.   Provided an example callback implementation that generates an HTML report with test statistics. Updated UI panel to provide a mechanism to explicitly connect to a JDBCSpyMBean (host/port). mplemented a table panel that will display statistics about recently executed SQL. HACK QueriesPerSecondPanel now supports basic replay from a log file. 11/30/07Quick implementation of a properties object.  The properties object should (fairly) generically handle JDBCSpy properties that have either been specified as System properties or as members of a &#39;jdbcspy.properties&#39; file. </p>

<p>See modules/jdbcspy-core/examples for jdbcspy.properties examples </p>

<p>What: </p>

<p>Added support for reading properties from a jdbcspy.properties file on the classpath Changed JDBCSpyDriver.class to JDBCSpyDriver.wrappedDriver </p>

<p>11/12/07Implemented automatic resets and file-based logging. </p>

<p>What: </p>

<p>Initial support for enabling / disabling statistics gathering. JDBCSpy can now optionally write queries to a file. New JDBCSpyDriver.logFile connection url parameter QueriesPerSecondPanel now periodically clears itself.</p>

 title : The kairos Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Kairos is a Pixlib extension that mainly rework on the transitions package to offer a new way to handle animations in your projects. </p>

<p>The main idea behind that project is that when we build animations in our games, sites, or applications, the speed of animations may changes according to the browser and/or the computer performances. Why not having a framerate-independant animation system ? Where tweens, movieclips and games routines always run at the same speed, even if framerate is different than the compiled one. </p>

<p>To realize that, all animated objects use a time bias in their algorithm. Basically, at each frame, objects compute animations according to the last frame duration. In that way, animations are not define in terms of unit/frames as we used to do, but as unit/seconds. </p>

<p>Please look at the wiki to a detailled description of Kairos mechanism and components.</p>
 summary : <p>Kairos³ is a Lowra extension that mainly rework on the transitions package, it’s offer a new way to handle animations in your projects. </p>

<p>The main idea behind that project is that when we build animations in our games, sites, or applications, the speed of animations may changes according to the browser and/or the computer performances. Why not having a framerate-independant animation system ? Where tweens, movieclips and games routines always run at the same speed, even if framerate is different than the compiled one. </p>

<p>To do that, all animated objects include a time bias in their algorithm. Basically, at each frame, objects compute animations according to the last frame duration. In that way, animations are not define in terms of unit/frames as we used to do, but as unit/seconds.</p>

 title : The maptrick Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Hattrick is a web-based football team management game, involving selling and buying players, making lineups, arranging friendly games and such. </p>

<p>Besides the appealing competitive aspects of the game, the community behind Hattrick is thriving. People from all over the world convene in the internal forum to discuss pretty much anything, whether related to the game or not. This community aspect drives some people to create websites with statistics about the game, and back in 2003, Maptrick was one such website. Originally envisioned as a &quot;graphical overview of where Hattrick players live in the world&quot;, it developed into something else. Over time, it evolved the following features: </p>

<p>- a historic overview of where ownerless teams existed in the league structure, and how the perceived problem of decreased competitivity increased over time - tracking of league growth and shrinkage over time - tracking of training type preference over time - Support for &quot;flag chasing&quot; (a form of meta-gaming where players arrange friendly matches with teams from countries that their team has never visited before) - the &quot;Hall of Cool&quot;, showing which teams have the &quot;coolest&quot; flags&quot; - a &quot;friendly suggester&quot; that makes it easier to find teams that will give you a flag </p>

<p>Unfortunately, Maptrick was forced to move from the server that it was hosted on, before it could be moved to the servers of fellow statistics service, Alltid. The cause was simple: Maptrick was created as a hobby project, and contains lots of sub-par code and queries, and lacks good documentation, which both precipitated its ejection from the (shared) server and made it harder to port to the (already strained) Alltid servers. </p>

<p>Now that Maptrick is in limbo between the original server and Alltid, and no end is in sight because of time restraints on the part of the developers, a possible solution presented itself: open the source to the public, so that people who do have time may make the code suitable for a production server, and maybe even add a feature or two. </p>

<p>If you think you can help, and you want write access to the repository, send an e-mail to CHPP-ste1n (laszlo.vandenhoek@gmail.com). Depending on public interest, I will add documentation that may ease development. </p>

<p>Documentation is mostly lacking, but for now you can start at [Architecture]. Further documentation will be provided as soon as someone asks for it.</p>

 title : The openepi Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Openepi is a JavaScript and HTML framework for statistical calculators.  It has more than 20 modules providing epidemiologic statistics for clinical and public health use with summary data.  Because Openepi consists entirely of client-side code, it can be downloaded and run from disk or run from the website.  The current version stores data in Windows by using an .HTA wrapper, but future plans call for enhanced data storage, and more statistics. </p>

<p>OpenEpi? provides statistics for counts and measurements in descriptive and analytic studies, stratified analysis with exact confidence limits, matched pair and person-time analysis, sample size and power calculations, random numbers, sensitivity, specificity and other evaluation statistics, R x C tables, chi-square for dose-response, and links to other useful sites. </p>

<p>OpenEpi? is free and open source software for epidemiologic statistics. It can be run from a web server or downloaded and run without a web connection. A server is not required. The programs are written in JavaScript? and HTML, and should be compatible with recent Linux, Mac, and PC browsers, regardless of operating system. A new tabbed interface avoids popup windows except for help files. </p>

<p>Test results are provided for each module so that you can judge reliability, although it is always a good idea to check important results with software from more than one source. Links to hundreds of Internet calculators are provided. </p>

<p>The programs have an open source license and can be downloaded, distributed, or translated. Some of the components from other sources have licensing statements in the source code files. Licenses referred to are available in full text at OpenSource?.org/licenses. OpenEpi? development was supported in part by a grant from the Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation to Emory University, Rollins School of Public Health. </p>

<p>A toolkit for creating new modules and for translation is included. Please let us know if you would like to collaborate in this way. Suggestions, comments, and expressions of interest in contributing to this effort should be sent by email to: andy.dean@gmail.com, cdckms@sph.emory.edu, and msoe@sph.emory.edu</p>

 title : The rdistplot Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The cornerstone of applied statistics seems to be hypothesis testing. Can a population be modeled by some distribution? What&#39;s the p value? </p>

<p>However visual comparison to actual distribution data may also yield interesting insights not possible with testing various hypothesis, since a hypothesis test is but one facet of a feature of a distribution versus actual data. </p>

<p>This package attempts to make it easier to use visual inspection for comparison. In no way will visual comparison be sufficient for data analysis, but it is an important part. </p>

<p>The rdisplot package provides methods to plot quantiles and densities of experimental data versus theoretical values (qq plots with enhancements). </p>

<p>This package is in alpha stage, and under active development.</p>

 title : The reflecxx Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Reflecxx is a simple tool for generating type information for C/C++ code.  It works by translating debugging information in object files into C data structures that can be linked into your program.  Type information is only generated when it is referenced in your source code, so extraneous data will not be included.  For example, if you wanted to convert an enumerated value to a string, you would declare the type and an external reference to the type information to be generated: </p>

<p>  enum hw_enum_t { HELLO_WORLD };
<br/>  extern struct reflecxx_full_type hw_enum_t_type_info;Then, to convert the value, you would use the reflecxx_enum_by_value() function: </p>

<p>  printf(&#39;%s\n&#39;, reflecxx_enum_by_value(&amp;hw_enum_t_type_info, HELLO_WORLD)-&gt;
<br/>	   ree_name);To generate the type information, first, you would compile the file and then run reflecxx-gen: </p>

<p>  $ gcc hw.c -c -o hw.o
<br/>  $ reflecxx-gen hw.o &gt; hw-type-info.c
<br/>  $ gcc hw-type-info.c hw.o -o hw
<br/>  $ ./hw
<br/>  HELLO_WORLDFeaturesJSON compatibility for writing out and reading in values. C/Invoke compatibility for functions.</p>

 title : The sqlim Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Русский: </p>

<p>Программа SqLim предназначена для системных администраторов небольших организаций, имеющих задачу контроля использования ресурсов Интернет сотрудниками организации и учета потребляемого интернет-трафика. Программа собирает статистику об интернет активности пользователей из логов прокси-сервера Squid. </p>

<p>Пользователи имеют возможность просмотра собственной статистики за выбранный интервал времени через web-интерфейс. При использовании basic-авторизации у пользователя имеется возможность менять свой пароль для squid через web-интерфейс. </p>

<p>Администратор SqLim может просматривать общую статистику и подробную статистику по каждому пользователю, вводить ограничения на размер месячного трафика пользователя, при использовании basic-авторизации управлять списком пользователей через web-интерфейс. </p>

<p>Настройки программы позволяют: </p>

<p>использовать два вида авторизации пользователей: basic и ntlm. хранить информацию о доступе в интернет за произвольный период времени задавать опциональный список сайтов, для которых траффик суммируется не по полному имени домена, а по домену заданного (обычно второго) уровня, т.е. i36.odnoklassniki.ru, i51.odnoklassniki.ru не показываются отдельными строчками, а выводиться их сумма как odnoklassniki.ru иметь список пользователей, обладающих правами администратора, но без возможности изменять лимиты трафика других пользователей, их отображаемые имена, создавать/удалять пользователей и менять их пароли при basic-аторизации. отображать величину трафика в байтах либо мегабайтах </p>

<p>Модули программы написаны на Perl и sh, поэтому теоретически программу можно заставить запускаться на любой платформе, где имеются perl, apache, squid, mysql и возможность запуска скриптов по расписанию. Практически тестировалось на CentOS Linux. </p>

<p>Загрузить программу можно со страницы загрузки. История версий программы доступна здесь. Имеется краткая документация по установке, настройке и использованию. Замечания и предложения по улучшению программы просим направлять сюда. </p>

<p>English: </p>

<p>Collect statistics about users Internet activity and show it through web interface. Set traffic limit per user.</p>

 title : The statistics-contingency Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The Statistics::Contingency class helps you calculate several useful statistical measures based on 2x2 &quot;contingency tables&quot;.  I use these measures to help judge the results of automatic text categorization experiments, but they are useful in other situations as well. </p>

<p>The general usage flow is to tally a whole bunch of results in the Statistics::Contingency object, then query that object to obtain the measures you are interested in.  When all results have been collected, you can get a report on accuracy, precision, recall, F1, and so on, with both macro-averaging and micro-averaging over categories.</p>
 title : The statistics-distributions-js Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This library calculates percentage points (5 significant digits) of the u (standard normal) distribution, the student&#39;s t distribution, the chi-square distribution and the F distribution. It can also calculate the upper probability (5 significant digits) of the u (standard normal), the chi-square, the t and the F distribution. </p>

<p>These critical values are needed to perform statistical tests, like the u test, the t test, the F test and the chi-squared test, and to calculate confidence intervals. </p>

<p>This is a direct port of the Perl module Statistics::Distributions. </p>

<p>If you are interested in more precise algorithms you could look at: </p>

<p>StatLib: http://lib.stat.cmu.edu/apstat/ ;  
<br/>Applied Statistics Algorithms by Griffiths, P. and Hill, I.D. 
<br/>, Ellis Horwood: Chichester (1985)</p>

 title : The traintracker Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>PurposeThis project aims to develop a flexible training log application for desktop use.  It is  written in C++ with Qt4 libraries, supporting cross platform usage. </p>

<p>DetailsThe target audience includes runners of all ability levels, and especially those who enjoy varied activity.  This program provides a means to track many different types of activities (great for those unfortunate periods of injury), yet maintains a loose focus on running.  A jogger, new marathoner, or elite miler should all feel comfortable entering data, for the fields correspond to relevant aspects of daily training. </p>

<p>The current version supports a number of basic attributes when describing an activity, including: </p>

<p>Date Time Location Route Duration Distance Effort Splits, and  Notes While some of these attributes are more suitable for distance oriented activities, this logging application currently categorizes entries into the following: </p>

<p>Run Workout Race Bike Cycle Walk Rest Swim Lift Core, and  Other Once the data is entered, it is stored in a flexible and open database.  By querying this database, the application is able to allow for easy browsing.  Furthermore, by employing an enterprise-level database system, this program can powerfully manipulate the result set.  This allows the user to filter all logged activities by every attribute or keyword.   </p>

<p>In addition to this filtering mechanism, the application provides a powerful plotting tool.  By default, distance vs. time is plotted for the arbitrary selected set, however an extensive plotting library exists.  One can imagine plotting duration or effort vs. time, distance vs. effort, or even duration vs distance vs effort. </p>

<p>Integration with an online street map/desktop globe is also provided.  This allows a user to accurately calculate a recent run.  It is planned that future versions will allow users to save and load custom routes.  Such a feature would simplify data entry, and perhaps give greater meaning to the splits of common runs. </p>

<p>Technical features Developed with Qt4.4 and gcc C++  XML configuration file  SQLite local database  MySQL remote database  database format well-defined and open to 3rd party interaction  therefore, multiple conceivable user interfaces (CLI, QT, GTK)  also, web publishing with a LAMP stack Future goals integration into modern, existing technologies, including Facebook  generalization of design to minimize running focus  generalization of code to allow for greater database support  define a split descriptor language for machine parsing</p>

 title : The ttext Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A collection of programs, tools, functions, scripts and source code snippets cohesively packaged to make the daily lives of those who work with the Teradata database easier in as many respects as possible. </p>

<p>This project currently contains the following items: </p>

<p>User Defined FunctionsORDERED_CONCAT() </p>

<p>Have you ever written a procedure or script that generates SQL, and wanted to generate an ordered list of columns?  Did you end up writing an ugly FOR loop in Teradata SPL? </p>

<p>The ORDERED_CONCAT aggregate function will combine input values with a delimiter ordered by a value you specify.  Try it out using a statement like this! </p>

<p> SELECT
<br/>   &#39;SELECT &#39; ||
<br/>   ORDERED_CONCAT(TRIM(ColumnName), &#39;, &#39;, ColumnID) || 
<br/>   &#39; FROM &#39; || TRIM(DatabaseName) || &#39;.&#39; || TRIM(TableName)
<br/> FROM
<br/>   DBC.Columns
<br/> GROUP BY
<br/>   DatabaseName
<br/> , TableName
<br/> ;SECONDS() </p>

<p>This set of functions will convert INTERVAL values into a total number of seconds.  Useful for downstream calculations on the difference of two TIMESTAMP values: </p>

<p> SELECT
<br/>   StartTime                                         (TITLE &#39;Start&#39;)
<br/> , FirstRespTime                                     (TITLE &#39;Response&#39;)
<br/> , SECONDS(FirstRespTime - StartTime DAY TO SECOND)  (TITLE &#39;Elapsed&#39;)
<br/> FROM
<br/>   DBC.DBQLogTbl
<br/> WHERE
<br/>   StartTime IS NOT NULL AND FirstRespTime IS NOT NULL
<br/> SAMPLE
<br/>   15
<br/> ;ViewsTableStats </p>

<p>This view provides an easy-to-query list of all statistics that have been collected in your environment.  Includes the last date and time statistics were collected, and the number of rows that the table / join index / hash index had at the time statistics were collected.  Also shows all indexes that do not have statistics collected. </p>

<p>  DatabaseName
<br/>  TableName
<br/>  TableKind
<br/>  ColumnList
<br/>  StatsCollectedFlag
<br/>  LastCollectionDate
<br/>  LastCollectionTime
<br/>  NumRowsDuringLastCollect
<br/>  IndexName
<br/>  IndexNumber</p>

 title : The wivet Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>WIVET is a benchmarking project that aims to statistically analyze web link extractors. In general, web application vulnerability scanners fall into this category. These VAs, given a URL(s), try to extract as many input vectors as possibly they can to increase the coverage of the attack surface.  </p>

<p>WIVET provides a good sum of input vectors to any extractor and presents the results. In order an input extractor to run meaningfully, it has to provide some kind of session handling, which nearly all of the decent crawlers do. </p>

<p>As a side note, you don&#39;t have to (though encouraged) download and setup your own WIVET. (You can basically visit WGT Page). Just make sure you read usage page first! </p>

<p>WIVET v3 is released (Try the SVN for up-to-date teasers...)</p>

 title : The yabzs Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Yet another nio framework for javaYanf4j is another nio framework for java,it is light weight,simple and have a great performance.It only supports non-blocking mode for tcp/udp server and client,it doesn&#39;t supports blocking mode.It needs jdk&gt;=5.0. </p>

<p>ExampleA Time Server </p>

<p>import java.io.IOException;
<br/>import java.text.DateFormat;
<br/>import java.text.SimpleDateFormat;
<br/>import java.util.Date;</p>

<p>import com.google.code.yanf4j.nio.Session;
<br/>import com.google.code.yanf4j.nio.impl.HandlerAdapter;</p>

<p>public class TimeHandler extends HandlerAdapter{</p>

<p>	@Override
<br/>	public void onSessionStarted(Session session) {
<br/>		Date date = new Date();
<br/>		DateFormat dateFormat = new SimpleDateFormat(&quot;yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm:ss&quot;);
<br/>		session.asyncWrite(dateFormat.format(date));
<br/>		session.flush();
<br/>		session.close();</p>
 title : The yanf4j Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Yeti WitchThis project adds several well known techniques for finding strings-that-almost-match-other-strings to the native Javascript String object, some of which are phonetic algorithms. </p>

<p>The supported list currently includes Soundex, Refined Soundex, Metaphone, Caverphone, Levenshtein distance, anagrams and Porter Stemming. All of these are primarily designed to work with the English language, although anagrams and Levenshtein are just string analysis so will work with anything. </p>

<p>The extensions are primarily designed to be executed under the Rhino scripting engine although porting them to different interpreters (to run in the browser or whatever) should be trivial. </p>

<p>TestsAfter checking out (or downloading) the code you should probably execute the unit tests. This will determine whether your system will run the code. </p>

<p> svn checkout http://yeti-witch.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ yeti-witch-read-only
<br/> cd ./yeti-witch
<br/> java -jar js.jar test/run.jsTo run the tests without clocking the test times use the -noclock flag.  </p>

<p> java -jar js.jar test/run.js -noclockIf you want to use copy of Rhino in your classpath then remove the one distributed with Yeti. I&#39;ve tested it on Rhino1_7R2pre &amp; Rhino1_5, 1_6R7 running under OSX 1.4. </p>

<p>ExamplesThe anagram tool will compare two arguments and return a &#39;1&#39; if the strings are anagrams of one another, </p>

<p> // prints &#39;1&#39; - ie. is an anagram
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/anagram/is.js &#39;fawlty towers&#39; &#39;flowery twats&#39;You can print the Caverphone code of a given string, </p>

<p> // prints &#39;WK11111111&#39; 
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/caverphone/get_code.js &#39;witch&#39;The Levenshtein tool (AKA. edit distance) will return an integer representing the number of operations needed to transform a given string in to the second given string. </p>

<p> // prints &#39;1&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/levenshtein/distance.js &#39;beatls&#39; &#39;beatles&#39;Likewise, metaphone gives you the metaphone code for a given string. Providing a second argument will set the metaphone key length, which defaults to 4. </p>

<p> // prints &#39;LNTNLM&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/metaphone/get_code.js &#39;london olympia&#39; 6Porter&#39;s stemming algorithm will attempt to truncate spurious word endings in order to find word stems. </p>

<p> // these two words have the same stem, &#39;probabl&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/porter/stem.js &#39;probably&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/porter/stem.js &#39;probabilities&#39;There&#39;s also a utility to stem an input file of new-line-seperated words. </p>

<p> // prints a list of stemmed output 
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/porter/stem-file.js &quot;test/data/stemmer/input&quot;Both Soundex and Refined Soundex have utilities that (a), print the soundex code of a given string, </p>

<p> // prints, B342 and B10673
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/soundex/get_code.js &#39;beatls&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/soundex-refined/get_code.js &#39;beatls&#39;... and (b), a diff tool that, in Soundex&#39;s case return the number of characters that are the same in a two give soundex keys - and given the keys have a maximum length of 4 characters, 4 indicates an exact match while 0 a very inexact match, </p>

<p> // the soundex values differs slightly, so printed value is &#39;3&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/soundex/difference.js &#39;threw&#39; &#39;through&#39;</p>

<p> // The soundex values differs entirely, so the printed value is &#39;0&#39;
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/soundex/difference.js &#39;witch&#39; &#39;trumpet&#39;While in Refined Soundex&#39;s case the difference is expressed as a decimalised percentage of the difference between the two codes. </p>

<p> // prints 0.5, as their is a 50% difference in their Refined Soundex keys
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/soundex-refined/difference.js &#39;buzz&#39; &#39;fuzz&#39; // as above but reduce the key comparison to &#39;3&#39;, which prints 0.25
<br/> java -jar js.jar examples/soundex-refined/difference.js &#39;buzz&#39; &#39;fuzz&#39; 3XML LookupGiven some of the operations are time intensive it may be quicker to generate a one-off lookup file containing a pre-defined list of words translated to their phonetic codes. So, for each word in a given file the xml lookup tool will produce an xml sequence containing the various Yeti-Witch algorithms, </p>

<p> java -jar js.jar examples/lookup/xml.js &#39;dictionary/names.girls&#39;Using one of the shipped dictionaries this will print something like this,  </p>

<p> 
<br/>  
<br/>    AALIYAH
<br/>    AALIYAH     A400
<br/>    A070
<br/>    ALA1111111
<br/>    ALY
<br/>  
<br/>  
<br/>    ABBIE
<br/>    ABBIE
<br/>    ...
<br/> Anagrams and Levenshtein are excluded from this as they are both comparison operations that need a second (eg. user input) string. </p>

<p>&#39;Yeti Witch&#39; ?Yeti Witch is an anagram of White City, the area of London where I work. The anagram can be found on the Central Line of the London Underground anagram map - credit: Barry Heck ;) </p>

<p>Not MineThe Caverphone and Metaphone methods are both Javascript ports of the algorithms written for the Apache Codec project. Likewise the Porter Stemmer and Levenshtein code has been adapted from previously released examples. Credits for these works and license details can be found at the head of each file in the distribution.</p>

 title : The csharp-googlemaps Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This project aims to provide better integration of Google Maps with .NET applications.  It provides a set of C# classes and functions for creating Google Maps.  This interface attempts to adhere to the Javascript API as much as possible. </p>

<p>The basic usage is to build your maps in C# and then translate them to javascript with one function call.  You can also create parts of the map and translate them into Javascript - such as a set of markers.  This might be useful if creating a web service as the backend for an interactive map. </p>

<p>The code includes the C# library and an example application.  The library comes with a basic web control for getting started quickly, but you do not have to use the library this way. </p>

<p>This library does not support everything that the Javascript API provides, but is rather a rough sketch of Google Maps. </p>

<p>Example 1: MarkersHere&#39;s a basic example.  Let&#39;s show the google maps representation of a `for&#39; loop. </p>

<p>C# </p>

<p>Map map = mapControl.map;</p>

<p>for(float i=30; i-100; j--) {
<br/>		Marker m = new Marker(new LatLng((float)i, (float)j));
<br/>		map.addOverlay(m);
<br/>	}
<br/>}</p>

<p>addJavascript(mapControl.GetJavascript()); </p>

<p>Example 2: Info WindowsThe same example, but with some information windows with tabs. </p>

<p>C# </p>

<p>Map map = mapControl.map;</p>

<p>for(float i=30; i-100; j--) {
<br/>		Marker m = new Marker(new LatLng((float)i, (float)j));
<br/>		m.addInfoWindowTab(new InfoWindowTab(&quot;Profile&quot;, &quot;My name is Peter.\n&quot; +
<br/>			&quot;I am 23 years old.&quot;));
<br/>		m.addInfoWindowTab(new InfoWindowTab(&quot;Location&quot;, &quot;I live in the United States.&quot;));
<br/>		map.addOverlay(m);
<br/>	}
<br/>}</p>

<p>addJavascript(mapControl.GetJavascript());</p>

 title : The leafx Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>3D Racing game using the Microsoft XNA game engine using adaptive object technology.</p>
 summary : <p>Original lib3ds distribution can be found here: http://lib3ds.sourceforge.net</p>

<p>To build, you will need Visual C++ Express and Visual C# Express. Open the Visual Studio 2005 command prompt (from the Visual C++ start menu entry), cd to the checked out directory, and run &#39;make.bat&#39;. The wrapper dll and assembly will be placed in &#39;Build/Debug&#39; and &#39;Build/Release&#39; respectively.</p>

<p>To use, reference the Lib3dsNet assembly from your C# application. The Lib3ds.dll must be in the application working directory (the Lib3dsNet.dll assembly must be in the application startup directory), where it is normally copied if the &#39;Copy Local&#39; attribute is true in the IDE.</p>
 title : The lib3ds-csharp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>　　LightweightCTi是一套旨在帮助开发人员迅速构建语音相关应用的一套开放源代码的基础框架。LightweightCTIi最初是本人在开发公司语音催缴系统后抽象完成的一套供网上朋友参考的演示性项目，当时是使用Pascal语言完成的基础性工作，提供了较为全面的应用开发接口（API）及扩展机制以方便感兴趣的朋友进行完善，同时，在我的个人网站也提供了下载。当前版本的LightweightCTi是以.NET为开发环境完成的。 </p>

 title : The megarit Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>MEGARIT is a library to do efficient multiprecision integer arithmetic. The first implementation will be in C#.</p>

<p>The library offers operations and functions sufficient for a solid layer for mathematical applications or libraries which provide high-level functionality. It emphasizes on efficient internal implementations and will compare fine with the best libraries available.</p>

<p>The MEGARIT library provides three interfaces to the arithmetical kernel:</p>

<p>(1) C#-like style (operations).
<br/>(2) Java-like style (member functions).
<br/>(3) Assembler-like style (in-place operations).</p>

<p>The interfaces (1) and (2) are based on the concept of immutable integers, interface (3) is not.  Interface (3) provides mutable integers and thus will lower the memory management overhead in many applications. The freedom
<br/>to choose between mutable and immutable integers within the same framework will be appreciated by many developers. (Note that even the Java BigInteger library internally uses mutable integers though this feature is not exported!)</p>

<p>Nevertheless, a compile time option will be provided to exclude the use of mutable integers from the library for those who want to assure that only immutable integers are used.</p>

 title : The nagios-csharp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Several years ago, Erik Doernenburg created a type of ORM (Object-Relational Mapping) software named Neo.  </p>

<p>From the original project: </p>

<p>The .NET Entity Objects Framework
<br/>Neo is a framework for .NET developers who want to write enterprise applications with an object-based domain model. It is well suited for domain-driven design and agile development. 
<br/>Neo includes tools that create an extensible object-based domain model as well as the database schema from a an abstract description of the model. At run-time, rich schema information is used to dynamically generate all SQL required for object persistence management. Being based on ADO.NET data sets, a Neo domain model is independent of the actual backing store and works equally well with databases and objects in an XML representation. 
<br/>The last official release was in June 2006. Since then, several users have continued to use and improve Neo. This project, dubbed Neo2, is our effort to consolidate, update, and extend this most excellent development tool. </p>

<p>WhatsNewWishListExternalResourcesOriginal Neo Site</p>

<p>statement = conn.execute &quot;Select * from Users&quot; </p>

 summary : <p>mod_guarddog performs some basic input validation on every HTTP requests sent to the web server.  This validation checking can prevent over 70% of common cross-site scripting (XSS) issues from occuring. </p>

<p>The following validations are performed: </p>

<p>Look for start of tags (Look for onXYZ= Look for &amp;#...; Look for javascript: mod_guarddog is available for both Apache 2.0, 2.2 and IIS 6 and 7. </p>

<p>This is a drop-in mitigation for most cross-site scripting issues. </p>

<p>Types of cross-site scripting mitigated by mod_guarddog: </p>

<p>Tag injection into HTML.  ... Javascript: in URLs Injection of onXYZ handlers into HTML attributes No protection against: </p>

 title : The activitytones Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>MotivationThe introduction of the mobile phone has introduced modern society to widespread ubiquitous computing.  Yet the general overwhelming acceptance of mobile phones as a convenience and necessity is offset by a laundry list of prevalent inconveniences and annoyances. Not least of these problems with mobile phones is the amount of switching between ringtone volumes and types throughout the day.  Many people find it necessary to switch between high and low volume ringtones or between sound only, vibration only, and no ringtones multiple times every day.   This presents a few common problems for mobile phone users.  First, there is the annoyance of having to physically adjust the ringtone settings several times a day.   Then there is also a category of problems that summed up as inappropriate ringtones.  These generally arise from either forgetting to switch between different ringtone settings or not bothering to switch from one ringtone setting when it will be needed again shortly (e.g. during a ten minute break from class or work).  These inappropriate ringtones often cause one to miss a call when they have an opportunity to take it, or cause one to be disruptive when one is in a focused setting (e.g. at a business meeting or in class).   </p>

<p>ClaimAlthough many mobile phone designers have worked hard to make ringtone switching simple, but as of yet there is no widespread automated system for ringtone switching. There are a few methods of automating this system that are worthy of consideration.  Two systems that are common to ubiquitous computing would be time-based ringtone switching or location-based ringtone switching.  Both of these methods offer very practical ways of automating ringtone switching, but still require fairly regular input from the user and are prone to inappropriate ringtones as phone availability is not always clear cut in terms of a set of rules based on time and space.  We argue that to implement reliable ringtone switching, knowing where or when you are doing something isn’t as important as knowing what you are doing.   We hypothesize that the most appropriate ringtone is based on the level of physical activity one is involved in at the time of the call.  For example: if one is involved in a high level of activity (such as walking), then a loud ringtone is usually appropriate.  Inversely, if one is involved in a low level of activity (such as sitting), then a quiet ringtone (including vibration only and no ringtone) is appropriate.   If such a system can be implemented to within a certain level of accuracy, then we believe that with only basic calibration and some very infrequent adjustments, activity-based ringtone switching has real potential for being the basis of completely automated ringtone switching.  In other words, this very basic system will act as the initial proof-of-concepts for a product-level activity-based ringtone switching system. </p>

<p>Solution ApproachAlthough most mobile phone manufacturers do not include “activity level sensors” in their phones, the Apple iPhone offers a convenient platform for prototyping such a system.  The iPhone comes with an onboard accelerometer that can be used to measure changes in acceleration as well as general orientation of the phone.  In order to prove the concept of an activity-based ringtone switching application, we would like to start with an exploratory study based on a simple iPhone application that varies the volume of a noise based on perceived level of activity during simulated phone calls.  These simulated phone calls will occur on some provided time interval (either random or user defined) for testing and demonstration purposes.   We plan on creating a very simple application providing basic sound playback, user customizability for testing, and data retrieval for statistical analysis.  The purpose of this study will be to determine feasibility an activity-based ringtone switching system.  We will measure the feasibility of this system based on creating an application that simulates the accuracy of such a system and observation made on the effectiveness of these simulations.</p>

 title : The bourre Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Bourre or Boo-Ray is a trick based card game originating in Louisiana.It is similar in play to Spades and Euchre.  Like many card games the rules vary from game to game.A typical Bourre game goes like this. </p>

<p>An ante is placed into the pot by all players.  The dealer deals 5 cards to each player. After dealing and before looking at his cards, the dealer is flips face up one of his cards to determine the trump suite that will be used by everyone during the game. At this point each of the players decide in a clockwise fashion starting just left of the dealer if they are in, out, or check. Once a single player is in, the check option is no longer available. Players that drop are out for the duration of this particular game which could be many hands. Players that remain in are allowed to draw new cards by discarding a like number. Due to the deck only having 52 cards, a game of 7 allows each player to  draw 2 and a game of 6 allows each player to  draw 3.  If there are 5 or fewer players, each player can draw up to 5 cards.  Once the draw is complete, the player to the left of the dealer starts the game by leading a card. The next player must play a card of the same suite if he has one, otherwise he can &quot;throw off&quot; another suit or &quot;trump&quot; the played suite. The highest card of the led suite wins the trick unless trump cards are played. If trump cards are played, the highest trump card would win the trick. Aces are the highest cards and 2&#39;s are the lowest.  Any player not winning a single trick must match the pot.  Any player winning three tricks wins the pot.  If one ore more players match the pot, the game continues even if someone gets 3 tricks since this money replaces the pot.   If no one gets 3 tricks to win the game, a round a ante&#39;s occurs and  another game is dealt by the person on the left of the dealer.  The deal rotates in a clockwise rotation.  The game ends when two players remain and one player gets 3 or 4 ticks and the other player gets 1 or 2 tricks.    </p>

<p>Remaining goals are as follows: </p>

<p>Complete the game engine and run simulations using various styles of play to determine winning statistics Log these statistics to a mysql database Build a user interface on top of the game and be able to play on an iphone and website.  If you are a UI specialist and are interested in contributing to this project, please let me know.   </p>

<p>This project is being developed using Java (JDK 1.6) with a Maven 2 build environment.</p>

 title : The lumpsplit Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The long-term management of metapopulations were performed through simulations for a case study based loosely upon herring to the west of the British Isles. These stocks are currently assessed and managed by management area, although there is evidence of much mixing between stocks (in terms of connectivity, migrations and exploitation). The simulations test the sustainability of fishing under two hypotheses corresponding to either discrete stocks which only mix on the feeding grounds, or where diffusion between stocks takes place, and where the assessment process assumes either discrete stocks or one metapopulation. The study showed that assessment based upon virtual population analysis could fail to detect overexploitation of stocks and to detect and distinguish between the effects of exploitation and regime shifts.</p>

 title : The newcp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>I/O in applications has become the biggest bottleneck in desktops, scientific computing, large scale simulations etc. Improvement in CPU speeds has shown significant improvement as compared to improvement in disk and memory speeds. Multi-tasking in Operating Systems gives rise to multiple I/O streams. Unlike the shared resource, the CPU, multiple I/O  streams can actually degrade the performance of the disk. In this article, we present a simple case study where we look at multiple sequential I/O streams accessing the same disk and study the degradation in performance caused by this scenario. We further propose a simple solution to remedy this situation. Readers who study this article are more likely to realize how to improve the performance of simple applications running on their desktop. </p>

<p>We believe that any reader familiar with programming and using any Operating system such as Linux, AIX, Solaris etc can immediately grasp the underlying idea and benefit from it. </p>

<p>We based our project on the coreutils package. We modified the existing file &quot;copy.c&quot;, and added a header file, both of which can be found in the &quot;Source&quot; repository. </p>

<p>A full report of our project, explaining the idea, its implementation and the description and results of all the tests we ran, is available in the download section.</p>

 title : The packmol Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>PackmolThis page contains the version history of Packmol. You can download packmol from this page, but give preference to the official Packmol page, for which the link is provided here. </p>

<p>What is PackmolPackmol creates an initial point for molecular dynamics simulations by packing molecules in defined regions of space. The packing guarantees that short range repulsive interactions do not disrupt the simulations. </p>

<p>The great variety of types of spatial constraints that can be attributed to the molecules, or atoms within the molecules, makes it easy to create ordered systems, such as lamellar, spherical or tubular lipid layers. </p>

<p>The user must provide only the coordinates of one molecule of each type, the number of molecules of each type and the spatial constraints that each type of molecule must satisfy. </p>

<p>The package is compatible with input files of PDB, TINKER, XYZ and MOLDY formats. </p>

<p>See the  Packmol&#39;s Home Page for more information. </p>

<p>ReferencesPlease always cite one of the following references in publications for which Packmol was useful: </p>

<p>L Martinez, R Andrade, EG Birgin, JM Martinez, Packmol: A package for building initial configurations for molecular dynamics simulations. Journal of Computational Chemistry, 30, 2157-2164, 2009. (link to journal) </p>

<p>JM Martinez, L Martinez, Packing optimization for the automated generation of complex system&#39;s initial configurations for molecular dynamics and docking. Journal of Computational Chemistry, 24, 819-825, 2003. (link to journal)</p>

 summary : <p>PathwayAnalyser (PA) is a tool for systems biologists for analysis of metabolic pathways, particularly by Flux Balance Analysis and ODE simulation.
