 title : The projet-csr-cpp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Projet CSR C++`Comment se compliquer la vie pour simplifier un projet.&#39; :) </p>

<p>Ce projet a pour but de reconstruire le projet CSR, option en 2e semestre de Licence 2 PCGI Option Informatique jusqu&#39;en 2007/2008. En dernière année avant une réforme fatale, nous fûmes la dernière promo à qui on a confié ce projet. </p>

<p>CSR?Conception de Systèmes Réactifs. Ce cursus avait comme objectif d&#39;apprendre les bases de la programmation orientée objets, des diagrammes UML, des algorithmes de recherche de chemin, de machines à états (automates, ou Finite State Machines)... tout ceci pour pouvoir entreprendre le projet CSR. </p>

<p>Ce projet regroupait donc tout ce que nous avions appris pour modéliser un comportement &quot;intelligent&quot; pour des entités simulées dans un environnement virtuel. </p>

<p>Ici, il s&#39;agissait de robots qui parcouraient et exploraient un labyrinthe plus ou moins complexe, à la recherche de clefs nécessaires pour ouvrir une Star-Gate, le but final. </p>

<p>La carte était parsemée de points de recharge qui pouvaient être piégés, et les robots perdaient de l&#39;énergie et se réchauffaient, et devaient donc coopérer pour atteindre le but. </p>

<p>Pourquoi reconstruire?Le projet d&#39;origine devait être programmé avec un langage appelé oRis, un langage développé par Fabrice Harrouet, et à la fois orienté objets et orienté agents. </p>

<p>ORis est un langage script et est conçu pour les simulations de mondes virtuels à base d&#39;entités autonomes, et est donc de très haut niveau et plus lent qu&#39;un programme compilé.  </p>

<p>De plus, le projet oRis a été délaissé, certaines fonctionnalités sont difficilement implémentées et et les binaires n&#39;étaient pas compatibles avec Windows, et pas toujours compatibles avec MacOS et Linux. </p>

<p>Nous avons donc décidé de refaire ce projet, pour produire un environnement/framework uniquement pour ce genre de simulation (cf §&quot;CSR?&quot;), avec un coeur compilé et rapide, et une implémentation par script dans un langage de niveau plus bas et plus généralisé.</p>
 title : The projetsmant Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Système multi - agents Le TP (du 05/11/08) consistera à commencer ce projet. Le Bureau d&#39;étude consistera à poursuivre ce projet aussi loin que possible. Le projet devra être rendu dans la semaine du 24-28/11/08 avec une exécution de votre programme prévue le Lundi 24/11/08 de 8h à 10h. Vous enverrez par mail à F.Evrard (evrard@n7.fr) l&#39;exécutable (au besoin ZIPé ou TARé) de votre programme (Matlab, éventuellement Java ou ...) ainsi que les fichiers résultats (divers graphiques et courbes) en formats imprimables. Dans tous les cas, que le projet soit programmé en Matlab ou bien utilise un autre langage (par exemple Java), vous   joindrez  un   fichier   de  configuration  d&#39;un   PC   sous   Windows   XP (positionnement de variables comme le PATH, ...) permettant de lancer votre application (par exemple, joindre la ligne de code à taper dans la fenêtre &quot;Invite de commandes&quot; ou la procédure d&#39;appel de votre application Matlab, ...). L&#39;évaluation de ce BE tiendra le plus grand compte de la facilité d&#39;emploi de votre application, de son autonomie : l&#39;évaluateur ne devra pas s&#39;&quot;embêter&quot; à configurer à la main son système pour être en mesure de constater que votre application ne marche pas. Le bureau d&#39;étude est à réaliser en binôme. Les noms des auteurs devront apparaître clairement tant dans le rendu papier que dans les mails. </p>

<p>Projet 
<br/>d&#39;Intelligence Collective </p>

<p>0. Définir un espace 2D (E2D) sous forme d&#39;une grille de dimension 50 cases x 50 cases. </p>

<p>1. Simuler la marche aléatoire d&#39;un agent partant d&#39;un point quelconque de cette grille en se dirigeant vers l&#39;un des 8 voisins (laisser une trace de toutes les cases parcourues pour 1000 pas, par exemple, d&#39;itération. (note 1) </p>

<p>2. Disposer, aléatoirement sur E2D, 650 ressources de 3 types différents (notés r1, r2, r3) et équiprobables. (note 2) </p>

<p>3. Définir la fonction sensorielle &quot;capteur&quot; de cet agent qui renvoie le nombre de ressources de type rx (pour chaque x=1,2,3) présentes parmi les 8 voisines de la position où il se trouve. (note 3) </p>

<p>4. Procéder à une marche aléatoire de cet agent          et  tracer  les   3  courbes histogrammes des ressources rencontrées. (note 4) </p>

<p>5. Définir 3 comportements pour cet agent : </p>

<p>- marche aléatoire de l&#39;agent vers une case voisine de là où il se trouve (déjà vu précédemment). </p>

<p>- prise par l&#39;agent, là où il se trouve, d&#39;une ressource en proportion inverse à sa fréquence parmi les 8 voisins : prob = 0 si freq = 8, prob = 1 si freq = 0 (à condition que l&#39;agent n&#39;ait pas déjà pris quelque chose et que la ressource se trouve là). </p>

<p>- pose par l&#39;agent, là où il se trouve, d&#39;une ressource proportionnellement à sa fréquence parmi les 8 voisins : prob = 1 si freq = 8, prob = 0 si freq = 0 (à condition que l&#39;agent ait une ressource &quot;en main&quot; et que la place soit libre). (note 5) </p>

<p>6. A chaque temps de cycle un seul de ces 3 comportements est effectuable {wa = walk, tx = take(rx), px = put(rx)}. Produire graphiquement la marche aléatoire de l&#39;agent, la liste des comportements enchaînés lors de la marche de cet agent et la liste des types de ressources rencontrées lors de cette marche (sur une centaine de cycles environ). (note 6) </p>

<p>7. Définir suffisamment d&#39;agents (tous caractérisés par les 3 comportements décrits en (question 5)) et les lancer dans des marches à partir de positions initiales aléatoires dans l&#39;espace ETD rempli de ressources, de sorte à faire apparaître des tas de ressources du même type. (note 7) </p>

<p>8. Définir un champ d&#39;attraction linéaire dans E2D (par exemple de gauche à droite) dont les cases alentour de celle de l&#39;agent sont d&#39;autant plus attractives qu&#39;elles se rapprochent du bord droit de E2D. Le rôle de ce champ est de modifier la probabilité de se diriger vers 1 des 8 voisins d&#39;une case donnée (jusqu&#39;ici walk s&#39;effectuait vers 1 des 8 voisins tous équiprobables). (note 8) </p>

<p>9. Procéder à une marche aléatoire pour un agent dans ce nouvel E2D (sans ressource mais avec champ linéaire attractif droit) à partir d&#39;une case initiale quelconque mais fixée au départ. Réitérer de telles marches en partant de cette même case initiale. Laisser une trace de toutes les cases parcourues au terme de toutes ces marches (effectuer une ou deux dizaines de marches). (note 9) </p>

<p>10. Transformer ce champ (statique) en un autre dynamique en définissant un comportement supplémentaire de l&#39;agent : </p>

<p>- marquer (d&#39;une unité de marquage) chaque case empruntée par l&#39;agent dans une marche aléatoire. (note 10) </p>

<p>11. Procéder à un lacher d&#39;un certain nombre d&#39;agents, aléatoirement positionnés initialement dans l&#39;espace E2D rempli de ressources. Produire l&#39;espace final, résultant d&#39;un nombre suffisant d&#39;itérations, pour voir apparaître des tas et des chemins privilégiés. (note 11) </p>

<p>12. On tentera de rendre les unités de marquages présentes en chaque case &quot;évaporables&quot;. On procèdera alors à un lacher comme en (question 11). (note 12) </p>

<p>13. On envisage l&#39;extension suivante : passage de dim(E2D) = 50x50 à dim(ET2D) = 1000x1000 (par exemple). On évaluera la difficulté de la chose et on proposera une méthode pour remédier éventuellement à ces difficultés. </p>

<p>14. On envisage la disparition progressive des ressources (qu&#39;elles soient dans un tas ou non) au cours du temps et apparition aléatoire d&#39;une même quantité de ressources. On regardera quelle influence ce phénomène a sur les simulations précédentes. </p>

<p>15. On envisage la visualisation des agents (et pas seulement des traces de leurs déplacements) sur la grille représentant E2D et la gestion en temps réel (à chaque instant du cycle) de leurs positions (ie: les voir se déplacer). </p>

<p>16. On souhaite disposer d&#39;une interface d&#39;utilisation conviviale de définition, de paramétrage, d&#39;exécution, d&#39;interruption et d&#39;affichage des résultats de cette application</p>
 title : The protohaptic Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ProtoHaptic: An Interactive Haptic Prototyping Tool  </p>

<p> </p>

<p>More screenshots... </p>

<p>What is ProtoHaptic?ProtoHaptic is an interactive haptic prototyping application which supports SensAble haptic devices. </p>

<p>The program is built upon the existing OpenHaptics APIs and facilitates the interactive construction and manipulation of a three dimensional environment that can both be seen on screen and felt via the force feedback haptic device. </p>

<p>Primitive objects may be added and positioned in the scene and various familiar transformations such as scaling and rotation applied to them. In addition to the usual geometric operations the editor provides the ability to change the haptic properties of the scene such as the stiffness of an object, or the lateral friction produced by a surface. </p>

<p>It is intended that the final product will provide a user friendly alternative to programing, for the purposes of rapidly prototyping a haptic environment. </p>

<p>For more information, read on or check out the documentation (Project Report, Short Paper at HAID 2006, User Manual and more...) in the dowloads section. </p>

<p>Executables are also available in the downloads section, while the source code is available via SVN (details the source section). </p>

<p>FeaturesPrimitive Objects: Cube, Sphere, Cylinder, Triangle, Torus. Transformations: Translation, Scaling, Rotation and other object specific transformations. Real time editing of haptic properties: Stiffness, Static Friction, Dynamic Friction and Damping. Rigid body dynamics and collision detection for creating dynamic haptic scenes Export code for created scenes: C Code using OpenGL API, C++ Code using AbstractModel API Import code to create scene: C++ Code using AbstractModel API, C++ Code using GHOST API BackgroundProtoHaptic was originally designed and implemented as a project forming part of my undergraduate course at the University of Glasgow, supervised by Dr Steven A Wall. I now use the application fairly regularly as a tool for haptic research and development in my work at The Royal Veterinary College. I have continued to work on some features as and when I have required them. </p>

<p>Applications of ProtoHapticAlthough the applications of such an direct manipulation editor are deliberately as diverse as possible, it is envisaged that it would be particularly useful in the following scenarios. </p>

<p>The rapid prototyping of haptic interfaces for immediate user testing. The iterative development and refinement of specialist simulations by non-computing scientists. E.g. Medical/Veterinary training simulations. Prototyping experimental procedure, say in psychological research. Designing three dimensional models for use in external applications or games. Whilst working at The Royal Veterinary College as a software developer / haptic researcher, I have used ProtoHaptic for: </p>

<p>Allowing a vet student to develop a cat’s abdomen palpation simulator (without the need to learn how to program). Allowing another vet student to design haptic models for a haptic pulse simulator. Designing haptic models for other haptic applications written using the AbstractModel API. Converting old legacy GHOST code to AbstractModel API code using import/export features</p>
 summary : <p>Framework developed in java and will allow users to develop complex card game simulations. Also provides for access to previous poker simulations and poker games via postgres</p>
 title : The ptsim Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The ptsim2 Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Allows users to create simulations of card games</p>
 summary : <p>Developing an open-source Python implementation of the Fast Multipole Algorithm (FMM) for scientific applications.The FMM can be used in many scientific computing applications: the simulation of many stars, electrostatics, the calculation of atoms or molecules out of equilibrium, and particle methods for continuum problems. The advantages of the FMM can be huge when large numbers of particles are involved, as it reduces the complexity of calculations from O(N2) to O(N).  </p>

<p>A more widespread adoption of the FMM algorithm has not occurred, mainly due to the complexity of the algorithm and the considerable programming effort, when compared with other algorithms like particle-mesh methods, or treecodes providing O(N log N) complexity.  </p>

<p>We are developing an open source implementation of the FMM —with particular application to the calculation of a velocity field induced by N vortex particles. </p>

<p>February 2008 -- at this time, we release a stable alfa version of the Python code, and invite interested parties to email us if they would like to collaborate with us on further developments. </p>

<p>We distribute this code under the MIT License, giving potential users the greatest freedom possible.  We do, however, request fellow scientists that if they use our codes in research, they kindly include us in the acknowledgement of their papers.  We do not request gratuitous citations;  only cite our articles if you deem it warranted. </p>

<p>Related linksPetFMM: Open-sourced Parallel C++ implementation of the Fast Multipole Method. PetFMM can be obtained directly from its repository or from the group&#39;s webpage. </p>

<p>Publications&quot;Characterization of the errors of the FMM in particle simulations&quot;  by Felipe A. Cruz and L. A. Barba.  Preprint uploaded to ArXiv on 10 September 2008. 
<br/>Although the literature on the subject provides theoretical error bounds for the FMM approximation, there are not many reports of the measured errors in a suite of computational experiments.  We have performed such an experimental investigation, and summarized the results of about 1000 calculations using the FMM algorithm, to characterize the accuracy of the method in relation with the different parameters available to the user.  In addition to the more standard diagnostic of the maximum error, we supply illustrations of the spatial distribution of the errors, which offers visual evidence of all the contributing factors to the overall approximation accuracy: multipole expansion, local expansion, hierarchical spatial decomposition (interaction lists, local domain, far domain). This presentation is a contribution to any researcher wishing to incorporate the FMM acceleration to their application code, as it aids in understanding where accuracy is gained or compromised.  
<br/>&quot;Characterization of the accuracy of the fast multipole method in particle simulations&quot; This is the published paper, a revised version of the ArXiV preprint linked above. 
<br/>Published online: May 5, 2009.  DOI</p>
 title : The pyfmm Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>PyMacLab is the Python Macroeconomics Laboratory which serves the purpose of providing a convenience framework written in form of a Python library with the ability to solve non-linear DSGE models. The library supports solving DSGE models using 1st and 2nd order perturbation methods which are computed around the steady state. PyMacLab possesses the added advantage of being equipped with an advanced model file parser module, which automates cumbersome and error-prone linearization by hand. PyMacLab is written entirely in Python, is free and incredibly flexible to use and extend.</p>

 title : The r-vex Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ρ-VEX: A Reconfigurable and Extensible VLIW ProcessorThis is the project website for ρ-VEX, an open source VLIW processor with an accompanied development framework. The project started as the MSc project of Thijs van As. </p>

<p>About ρ-VEXρ-VEX is an open source reconfigurable and extensible Very-Long Instruction Word (VLIW) processor, accompanied by a development framework consisting of a VEX assembler, ρ-ASM. The processor architecture is based on the VEX ISA, as introduced by J.A. Fisher et al.. The VEX ISA offers a scalable technology platform for embedded VLIW processors, that allows variation in many aspects, including instruction issue-width, organization of functional units, and instruction set. The ρ-VEX source code is described in VHDL. ρ-ASM is written in C. </p>

<p>A software development compiler toolchain for VEX is made publicly available by Hewlett-Packard. The reasons VEX was chosen as the ISA are merely its extensibility and the quality of the available compiler. The design provides mechanisms that allow parametric extensibility of ρ-VEX. Both reconfigurable operations, as well as the versatility of VEX machine models are supported by ρ-VEX. The processor and framework are targeted at VLIW prototyping research and  embedded processor design. </p>

<p>The name ρ-VEX stands for &#39;reconfigurable VEX&#39; processor. Because the letter Rho (P or ρ) is the Greek analogous for the Roman R or r, ρ-VEX is pronounced as r-VEX. This is also the correct spelling when no Greek letters can be used (as is the case with the project website URL). </p>

<p>Getting StartedTo start experimenting with ρ-VEX, read the QuickstartGuide and download the latest code snapshot, or checkout trunk. When you have a Xilinx University Program Virtex-II Pro Board by Digilent, you should have ρ-VEX running within moments. </p>

<p>DocumentationThijs&#39; MSc Thesis with extensive documentation about ρ-VEX&#39; design and implementation ρ-VEX: A Reconfigurable and Extensible VLIW Softcore Processor (Presented on ICFPT&#39;08) QuickstartGuide OperationsSemantics instruction_layout.txt syllable_layout.txt Contact Information</p>

<p>Thijs van As  Computer Engineering Laboratory Faculty of Electrical Engineering, Mathematics and Computer Science Delft University of Technology Delft, The Netherlands</p>

 title : The anachronox-modding Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The best place to go to find out about Anachronox is the Wikipedia page.  If you still wish to find out more take a look at the Anachrodox. </p>

<p>No game assets are included here. </p>

<p>In order to work on these tools you will need to either download the demo and work with that or purchase one of the current budget releases of this game. In order to create a mod for Anachronox which others can play, you will need to purchase the game. This project currently includes the following elements: </p>

<p>AnoxToolsA Python library which allows reading many of the custom formats used for various purposes within the game data. </p>

<p>Most notably this includes a decompiler for the compiled APE game logic scripts.  As of the 9th of April 2007 this can be successfully used to decompile all the APE scripts which come with the game well enough to allow their recompilation with the script compiler the original game programmers released. </p>

<p>BspViewerA quick and dirty attempt at a viewer for the compiled BSP maps which come with Anachronox.  It was based on a version of the nedu 3D demo/game engine which wrapped PyOpenGL.  As such it is not readily usable and may require a bit of leg work to get it working. </p>

<p>nAnachronoxAn experiment to create a viewer for the custom Anachronox MD2 model format using the Nebula Device 3d engine.  It was taken far enough to exhibit standard model viewing functionality where a model could be viewed and rotated, so as to admire how much better it looked under Nebula than in the original Quake 2 derived game engine.</p>

 title : The battleship Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The beesiege Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The game idea is this. Life was good for the bees and their queen. They lived in their hive making honey and having fun. Until one day a spoiled little teenager threw his cigarette underneath the hive which caught on fire. Now the bees are left with no home and they have to travel through the forest to find a new place to live. But they are going to face a lot of challenges on their way… </p>

<p>The player controls the queen bee and her soldiers are following her at all times. Throughout the forest there are going to be a lot of enemies that will make the player’s life difficult. The queen is not able to attack, because that’s not her purpose in life, so she depends on her soldiers to protect her. Whenever an enemy is nearby the queen (player) will be able to select a number of bees and command them to destroy that enemy. The bees that survive the challenge will return to the queen. Of course many of them will die so a number of power ups is going to be distributed around the forest. When the queen makes it to the new hive the level ends. If the queen dies then it is game over. </p>

<p>Now just to give you an idea of how the game is going to look like, think of Wing Commander. Only replace the spaceship with the queen and the missiles with bees. Of course bees will not be shot at the enemy, they are going to move there at their own speed and attack him. </p>

<p>I am very excited about this project because it features various new stuff. First of all I do not know of any game that has a similar story / goal. Also I do not know of any game that uses this attack mechanism. Also the game features a very interesting animation mechanism. We use Behavioral Animation to move the bees around, which means that every bee or game character has a controller that generates forces and torques which drive the character. These forces and torques vary depening on the behavior that we are implementing. Behaviors include </p>

<p>Seek: the object travels to a target at maximun speed Arrival: the object travels to the target while slowing down until it reaches it Wander: the object moves in random directions within a radius Separation: the object is keeping a distance from its surrounding objects Allignment: the object follows the general direction of its neighbors The nice thing about these individual behaviors is that you can combine them and get more complex behaviors like Flocking where the objects form groups and also have a randomness to their movement like actual bird flocks. Behavioral Animation is not a new idea however what is original in our implementations is that these forces and torques that the controllers generate are given to Ageia’s PhysX which then takes care of the simulation and moves the objects. The effect of all that is very realistic movement.. You actually think that these are actual bees you see on the screen. </p>

<p>Another cool thing in my opinion will be the simplicity of the game. The player only controls the queen and everything else is AI. Of course it is more than that, the player will have to make decisions that will affect his chances of survival, but still the gameplay is very simple and fun.</p>

 title : The depsolver Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>NEWS (2008-11-10) Bugfix release 2.1 available for download in patch and full version forms. It fixes a mistake in the multipolar calculation of orders 2 and 3 for quadratic triangular elements. All previous versions have been marked as Deprecated to avoid confusion, but they are still available for download for those who need them for development purposes (go to downloads and select &quot;All Downloads&quot; then click &quot;Search&quot;). </p>

<p>DescriptiondepSolver is a Boundary Element Method solver for Laplace&#39;s  equation in 3D AC electrostatic problems. I originally wrote this program to study the characteristics of different dielectrophoretic trap designs. A big advantage of using this code to calculate dielectrophoretic forces is that the user can specify which approximation to use for the calculation of the force. In this manner, without having to change anything in the code, one can use a simple dipolar or quadrupolar approximation to quickly explore the force generated on a sphere over a large volume of space, or use the more general calculation based on the integration of the Maxwell&#39;s stress tensor over an arbitrarily shaped particle. </p>

<p>depSolver is convenient for dielectrophoretic force calculations, but it is in no way limited to them. It can be used to solve a wide variety of electrostatic problems as long as they involve conductors were the electric potential is specified and all dielectrics in the system can be considered as piecewise homogeneous. The source code is written in C and uses separate functions for most tasks in order to make modifications easier.</p>

 title : The elbowroom Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ElbowroomUsing procedural content generation techniques (PCG), Elbowroom will produce an enormous 3D world to explore. As the project develops, the world will become more detailed. It will take up very little disk space as the content will not be stored, but generated at runtime. It will be possible to reproduce the same world over and over or to generate new randomised worlds. </p>

<p>Elbowroom is implemented in Java and relies on the LWJGL and OpenGL. Early versions have been tested successfully on Windows XP, Windows Vista, and Ubuntu 8.10. </p>

<p>SetupElbowroom is not yet easy to run. There is yet no installer or executable. If you want to run Elbowroom from source, follow the instructions in setup.txt. I hope to make this easier in future once there is some worthwhile code written.</p>
 title : The ellipsoids Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Ellipsoidal Toolbox for MATLABEllipsoidal Toolbox (ET)  is a standalone set of easy-to-use configurable MATLAB routines to perform operations with ellipsoids and hyperplanes of arbitrary dimensions. It computes the external and internal ellipsoidal approximations of geometric (Minkowski) sums and differences of ellipsoids, intersections of ellipsoids and intersections of ellipsoids with halfspaces and polytopes; distances between ellipsoids, between ellipsoids and hyperplanes, between ellipsoids and polytopes; and projections onto given subspaces. </p>

<p>Ellipsoidal methods are used to compute forward and backward reach sets of continuous- and discrete-time piecewise affine systems. Forward and backward reach sets can be also computed for piecewise linear systems with disturbances. It can be verified if computed reach sets intersect with given ellipsoids, hyperplanes, or polytopes. </p>

<p>The toolbox provides efficient plotting routines for ellipsoids, hyperplanes and reach sets.   Required software: MATLAB 6.5 (or higher). </p>

<p>ET is also distributed as part of Multi-Parametric Toolbox (MPT). </p>

<p>Contact / Support Found ET useful for something?  Found a bug and wish to report it?  Have questions, suggestions or feature requests?  Wish to contribute to the ET development? Please, contact Alex Kurzhanskiy or report an issue. </p>

<p>In case you use ET in your research, we would greatly appreciate if you added the corresponding reference to your publications: </p>

<p>@techreport{Kurzhanskiy:EECS-2006-46,
<br/>    Author = {Kurzhanskiy, A. A. and Varaiya, P.},
<br/>    Title = {Ellipsoidal Toolbox},
<br/>    Institution = {EECS Department, University of California, Berkeley},
<br/>    Year = {2006},
<br/>    Month = {May},
<br/>    URL = {http://code.google.com/p/ellipsoids},
<br/>    Number = {UCB/EECS-2006-46}
<br/>}Download and Installation1. If you have a previous version of the toolbox installed, remove it completely. </p>

<p>2. Download ET or its lite version from the Downloads page. </p>

<p>3. Unzip the file into the directory where you want the toolbox to be. </p>

<p>4. Read the copyright notice. </p>

<p>5. In your MATLAB command window change the working directory to the one where you unzipped the distribution file and type: </p>

<p>      &gt;&gt; install6. At this point, the directory tree of ET is added to the MATLAB path list. In order to save the updated path list, in your MATLAB window menu go to File --&gt; Set Path… and click Save. </p>

<p>7. To get started, read the README file carefully. </p>

<p>Animations</p>

<p>Refinement of Ellipsoidal Approximation  It starts approximating the reach set with one external (blue) and one internal (green) ellipsoids, then the number of approximating ellipsoids is doubled – now there are two external and two internal, then it is doubled again – now there are four of each, finally, there are 32 external and 32 internal ellipsoids.   Switching System  The dynamics of the system changes every 5 seconds. For the first system, the external approximation is blue and internal – yellow; for the second, the external approximation is red and internal – green; for the third, the external approximation is magenta and internal – cyan. The set of initial conditions for the second system is the reach set of the first one, and the set of initial conditions for the third system – the reach set of the second one.   Switching System in 3D  Tthis example is similar to the previous one, only this time it is 3-dimensional system with one switch.   Reaching Boundary Point  This example illustrates how moving along the good curve using known control, we reach the boundary point of the reach set at given time.   Reaching Internal Point  By squeezing the set of controls and computing &#39;good curves&#39; for the squeezed set, we can steer the system to any internal point of the reach set at given time.   Choosing Control Based on Reach Set Information  The control can be chosen based on the reach set computed for the next time interval. Here, the black dot chooses where to go, knowing its reach set 5 seconds ahead. The reach set is displayed in red for external, and blue – for internal approximation.   Reach Set Info in 3D  This example is similar to the previous one, only in 3D.  </p>

<p>Third Party Software Packages in ETYALMIP - high-level MATLAB toolbox for rapid development of optimization code. 
<br/>SeDuMi - MATLAB toolbox for solving optimization problems over symmetric cones. 
<br/>Both packages are included in the ET distribution. So, you don’t need to download them separately. </p>

<p>Related SoftwareEllipsoidal Calculus based on Propagation and Fusion. Propagation is an operation of obtaining an ellipsoid that satisfies an affine relation with given ellipsoid. Fusion is operation of finding an ellipsoid that tightly bounds from outside the intersection of two given ellipsoids. 
<br/>Geometric Bounding Toolbox (GBT) - commercial MATLAB toolbox that deals with multidimensional convex and nonconvex polytopes and has a limited number of functions operating with ellipsoids. 
<br/>Hybrid System Tools - list of free modeling and verification tools for hybrid systems.</p>

 title : The levelwalker Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This plug-in will extract the geometry from a DeleD scene, and let you walk through it using WASD style keys. It will do collision detection with all geometry, except geometry marked as non-collidable. This allows you to get a better feel for what the level will look like from a player&#39;s perspective, without having to export it to a separate 3D engine. </p>

<p>Settings allow you to specify player height, and player radius, for putting the camera and collision in the right perspective. The player is modeled as a capsule with a small ray for feet (&quot;lollipop&quot; model). </p>

<p>Keys W - forward
<br/> S - backward
<br/> A - left
<br/> D - right
<br/> E - ascend
<br/> C - descend
<br/> space - jump
<br/> F - start floating (turn off gravity and collision testing)
<br/> G - stop floating (turn on gravity and collision testing)
<br/> ESC - quit the walkthroughInstallationUnzip the contents into your DeleD or Deled PRO folder. The three DLLs go in the same folder as deled.exe, the levelwalker plug-in goes in the plugins folder (it&#39;s arranged that way in the archive).</p>

 title : The mdlutility2 Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A 2D and 3D finite element formulation for modeling bulk metal forming procesess using a rigid-viscoplastic material model (flow formulation) was developed. Its main features are: it is based on an Eulerian description of the material flow implemented using the pseudo-concentration method; it allows the coupling of the elastic and thermo-elastic deformation of the forming tools and includes, in the model of material under deformation, the thermo-mechanical coupling. The developed formulation was implemented in the finite element code METFOR. This code was applied to the analysis of: the hot rolling of flat products, the vertical rolling of slabs (edging) and the hot upsetting of cylindrical samples. The features of this formulation, described above, were fundamental for the profile and flatness analysis of the hot rolled products because it is necessary to take into account the rolls deformation due to thermal and mechanical (bending and flattening) loading. The technological application of the developed formulation allowed its validation through the comparison of its predictions with the measurements performed by the process engineers of an industrial hot rolling mill.</p>

 title : The mini3d Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Mini3D is a simple 3D engine that runs in a Java applet </p>

<p>Models are based on geometric primitives: sphere, cone, cylinder, box. A model is passed to the applet in text mode, as a parameter. The text description is a concise vrml-like language, with motion and composite objects. </p>

<p>Sample codeSample code below for composite objects and motion. </p>

<p>{
<br/>  { box w=50 h=100 l=200 trn(-150,0,0) color(255,0,0) [rot(15,0,0)]  }
<br/>  { cylinder r=50 h=100 trn(-50,0,0) color(0,255,0) [rot(0,5,0)] 
<br/>    { cone r=20 h=40 trn(0,0,-70) rot(90,0,0) color(255,255,0) }
<br/>  }
<br/>  { cone r=50 h=100 trn0(0,50,0) trn(50,0,0) color(0,0,255) [rot(5,0,0)] }
<br/>  { [trn(0,0,5) step 10] [trn(0,0,-5) step 20]  [trn(0,0,5) step 20 goto 2]
<br/>    { sphere r=100 f=0.5 trn(150,0,0) color(0,128,128) [rot(0,3,0)] }
<br/>  }
<br/>}To doFor future developments I&#39;d like to add physics simulation. I already have implemented masses and gravity</p>

 title : The progressive-meshes Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>progressive-meshes is a surface simplification software which produces high-quality approximations of triangle progressive meshes models. It generates progressive meshes models with desired number of mesh faces or compression ratio, and every contraction is recorded in the generated file. Currently only core operators of .smf input file format are supported. </p>

<p>This is a C++ implementation of Michael Garland&#39;s Surface simplification using quadric error metrics and Hugues Hoppe&#39;s Progressive meshes. This software runs slower than Garland&#39;s Qslim, but the results are somehow better in details. Since every contraction is recorded, further usage of the generated .pm file could be extended, for example, building level-of-detail models or 3D streaming. </p>

<p>Credit goes to SU Tao for GUI. </p>

<p>InstallationVisit http://hezhao.net/project/progressive-meshes.html</p>

 title : The projetcsrrobots Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Lepton: A high-performance, pluggable particle engine and API for PythonLepton is designed to make complex and beautiful particle effects possible, and even easy from Python programs. </p>

<p>Lepton provides the following core features: </p>

<p>Native-code core for high-performance particle dynamics and rendering Pluggable particle controllers for specifying particle behavior Two pluggable OpenGL renderers, and two pygame renderers Spacial domains, used to control particle emission and behavior Easy to use and powerful texture support, including animation Modular architecture that lets you easily configure and customize the engine The code includes several examples of how you can use the engine (using pyglet and pygame). Note the engine itself does not depend on any other 3rd-party Python libraries and simply requires the application to setup an OpenGL context in order to render particles. </p>

 title : The pygalkin Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>3D-data in Astronomy means 2 spatial dimensions and one spectral dimension, i.e. having a spectrum for each pixel of your &#39;image&#39;. </p>

<p>This code is a loose collection of tools that uses numpy, pylab (former matplotlib) and scipy to handle these 3D-data, perform various operations on them and visualise them. Interactive classes are provided for manually manipulating certain routines. </p>

<p>The main use is to measure the kinematics of galaxies (therefore the name PyGalKin), both from Fabry-Perot observations of the H-alpha line and from integral field unit spectra. </p>

<p>The code is probably not usable without reading the source; documentation is lacking or non-existing. However, Python is highly readable and there should no high obstacles, especially for users of numpy, scipy and pylab, which become more and more common in astronomy as replacements for IDL and/or older data handling software. </p>

<p>Feel free to contact me at thomas.marquart at fysast dot uu dot se. </p>

<p>Note: This repository is not updated regularly (but I will regularly transfer the changes). It has moved to github: http://github.com/ivh/PyGalKin</p>

 summary : <p>A relatively simple game project developed in Java, featuring OpenGL and Swing implementations, as well as networking capabilities. </p>

<p>Timespan: 4 weeks. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>The gameThe &quot;Tic Tac Turn&quot;-game is loosely based on the famous &quot;Tic Tac Toe&quot;-game, but differs in the fact that the game is played on a 2x2 (or 3x3) field of individual &quot;Tic Tac Toe&quot;-boards, also referred to as blocks. With each turn, the player rotates a block clock- or counter-clockwise and puts his/her symbol on any of the available places. The game can be played with a maximum of 4 people, and the goal is to win by having 4 (for a 2x2 field) or 5 (for a 3x3 field) symbols in a row. </p>

<p>The implementationWe decided to put our OpenGL knowledge to the test and write a fully 3D version of the game in the time we had. The application is well-structed, contains a lot of documentation and follows the Model-view-controller design pattern. The OpenGL functionality is provided by JOGL, a low-level OpenGL wrapper for Java, and can be ran on any platform that is supported. </p>

<p>The application consists of two parts, which can be accessed by the launcher (see below): </p>

<p>Dedicated server: capable of hosting multiple games, handling challenges (requests from clients to join private games), kicking clients. Client: capable of querying and joining servers, single-player games (against the built-in AI player), multi-player games, challenging other clients, chatting, requesting hints, and more. </p>

<p>PreviewThe application&#39;s in-game view </p>

<p> </p>

<p>The application&#39;s launcher menu screen</p>

 summary : <p>Adaptive Virtual Environments have been developed aiming  at  generating  3D  environments  adapted  to user’s  necessities  and  interests.  Navigation  aid techniques  and  content  adaptation  improve  user interaction in such environments. This article presents a  system  for  supporting  real  time  adaptive  virtual environments.  title : The dockableflex Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The doze-xbmc-plugins Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A repository for my xbmc plugins, </p>
 summary : <p>Tools to read DVD-Video filesystems. </p>

<p>DVD-VideoA consumer video format used to store digital video on DVD-ROM discs. </p>

<p>File SystemThe basis for the DVD-Video filesystem is the Universal Disk Format (UDF) specification.  UDF defines data structures such as volumes, files, blocks, sectors, CRCs, paths, records, allocation tables, partitions, character sets and time stamps. </p>

<p>The UDF (ISO/IEC 13346, ECMA-167) specification was created by the Optical Storage Technology Association (OSTA). </p>

<p>File and Folder StructureThere may be up to two folders at the root level of the disk with the names VIDEO_TS and AUDIO_TS.  The files for a DVD-Video disk are in the VIDEO_TS directory.  The AUDIO_TS directory is reservered for DVD-Audio disks, another of the standards controlled by the DVD Forum. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>All of the files for a DVD-Video disk are in the single directory VIDEO_TS. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Video ManagerThe mandatory file VIDEO_TS.IFO contains the Video Manager (VMG) structures.  A backup is stored in the mandatory file VIDEO_TS.BUP. </p>

<p>Video Title SetEach DVD-Video disk may contain one or more distinct collections of video known as a Video Title Set (VTS).  A file named VIDEO_nn_0.IFO, where nn is the two digit number of the title, contains the Video Title Set structures. </p>

<p>Video ObjectA Video Object (VOB) is the container format for video, audio, subtitles and menus in DVD-Video.  It is a strict subset of the MPEG-2 Program Stream format. </p>

<p>Logical Structure </p>

<p>The logical structure of a DVD-Video divides it into titles. For example a disk might contain a feature movie in one title and a &quot;making of&quot; feature in a second title. There may be up to 99 titles. </p>

<p>Titles contain one or more chapters, otherwise known as parts. A chapter might represent a scene or an act in a film. There may be up to 999 parts in a title. </p>

<p>Each chapter contains one or more programs. Navigation is done using programs, a player command of &quot;previous&quot; or &quot;next&quot; selects the corresponding program. </p>

<p>Each program contains one or more cells. A cell is the smallest element used in authoring. </p>

<p>Cells contain many Video Object Units (VOBU). A VOBU is a self contained Group of Pictures in an MPEG program stream containing a few seconds of video. </p>

<p>The logical and physical data structures converge at the cell level. </p>

<p>Virtual MachineThe DVD-Video format allows for non-linear playback using graphical menus. A player implements a virtual machine (VM) which runs bytecode commands contained within Program Chains (PGC). </p>

<p>Each title contains up to 999 program chains. A PGC contains up to 99 programs. A program is an ordered collection of pointers to cells. A simple program chain may play the cells containing a film from start to finish. </p>

<p>A program chain may contain commands to be executed before playback of the first cell, after the playback of the last cell or before each cell. There may be up to 128 commands in a PGC. There may be commands and no programs and cells. A PGC with no commands and no programs and cells does nothing.</p>

 summary : <p>The project consists in develop a software that creates a link with FlightGear flight simulator over Telnet protocol and permits the control of a Cessna c172p (automatic fly by wire). </p>

 title : The flvbuilder Open Source Project on Open Hub

 title : The groovy-video-shop Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Build a resilient and robust distributed application that supports a simple order and fulfilment process for a chain of franchise video stores. </p>

<p>The video chain has shops and warehouses located across the country; and also has a central office that provides common services to the rest of the organisation. Customers can search for and order videos over the Internet, or go to their local store to browse and place orders for videos. Each store will run its own copy of the order process for handling locally-placed orders. Each warehouse will run its own copy of the delivery process to look after delivery requests it receives, and its own copy of the stock process to keep track of the goods it has on its shelves. Orders will be placed using a local store ordering system and result in delivery requests being sent to an appropriate warehouses which then will then send the ordered goods directly to the customer.</p>
 summary : <p>If you have a video that you would like to put on your iPod, you will most likely want to convert it to a compatible format, and you will most likely also want to lower its quality -- including shrinking the resolution of the video. </p>

<p>This is where this software comes into place. All you have to do is calculate the aspect ratio of your video, or even give the ratio on the form of either &quot;WIDTHxHEIGHT,&quot; &quot;width/height,&quot; or &quot;width:height,&quot; and tell it to iPodRes which will then give you suggestions on which resolution you should choose for your video when converting. </p>

<p>Note: This software is not a video converter, it just suggests video resolutions. </p>

<p>The requisites that the resolution calculator requires of the resolutions it suggests is that both the width and height values are evenly divisible by 8; that the height does not exceed 240 px (for videos where the width is greater than the height) and that the width does not exceed 320 (for videos where the height is greater than the width); and the suggested resolutions&#39; aspect ratio must not differ more than 5 % from the aspect ratio of the original video (or else it will start to look odd, so I&#39;ve read... somewhere). </p>

<p>The program will not choose a resolution for you -- you will have to do this yourself. (The program does however limit the suggestions to the five-percent aspect ratio error.) The reason for this is that the program cannot know whether a user prefers to have an aspect ratio as close to the original as possible, or if it would rather have a larger resolution for the video. So read the output and make the right decision for you! </p>

<p>Installation notes: </p>

<p>$ javac iPodRes.javaExamples: </p>

<p>1) $ java iPodRes 16:9
<br/>===== iPod VIDEO RESOLUTION CALCULATOR =====
<br/>Ratio: 16:9 = 1.7777777777777777</p>

<p>328 / 16:9 = 184, AR % error: 0.2717391304347838, res: 328x184
<br/>368 / 16:9 = 208, AR % error: 0.48076923076922906, res: 368x208
<br/>384 / 16:9 = 216, AR % error: 0.0, res: 384x216</p>

<p>2) $ java iPodRes 672x480
<br/>===== iPod VIDEO RESOLUTION CALCULATOR =====
<br/>Ratio: 7:5 = 1.4</p>

<p>336 / 7:5 = 240, AR % error: 0.0, res: 336x240In example 1) above, the ratio was given of the form &quot;width:height&quot;. We see that there are three suggestions in total: 328x184 with an aspect ratio error of about 0.27, which is fairly low; 368x208 with an AR % error of about 0.48, which is higher than the previous, although the resolution is larger which means higher quality. Now, I would pick AR over size, because the screen of the iPod is so small anyway, so I&#39;d take the first one if I had to pick between the two. Yet, there is one left: 384x216 with an AR % error of 0.0, which means it&#39;s a perfect resizing of the picture when it comes to maintaining the aspect ratio! And it so happens that it&#39;s the largest resolution of the three suggestions, so I shall pick that one! </p>

<p>In example 2), the ratio was given as a video resolution. In this case there is only one suggestion which fulfills the previously mentioned requisites: 336x240. It turns out that we were lucky this time, because as is visible, the error is zero, which means the original video&#39;s aspect ratio will be maintained with the suggested resolution! </p>

<p>Usage environment: I hope this software can come to use for someone. It&#39;s not too complicated at all; it&#39;s not really that fancy, but it does the trick for me. I use it in combination with a script I created that uses the free software &quot;ffmpeg&quot; to convert videos. I just feed the resolution of the original video to iPodRes, choose the best resolution according to my needs, then I feed the video file name and selected iPod video resolution to the script, and it does the encoding for me. </p>

<p>Feel free to copy, distribute or modify the software to your needs if you so wish. If you do, though, do so under the terms of the license, and, if you would, send me an e-mail with a patch of the changes and an explanation of what has been changed and why! :-) </p>

<p>Thanks, and happy usage!</p>

 title : The pagsegurodotnet Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>PagSeguro.NetAssista ao vídeo de exemplo de uso dos controles PagSeguro.Net </p>

<p>PagSeguro.Net é um conjunto de controles para ASP.NET que permite integrar sua aplicação de forma simples e segura ao sistema de pagamento online do UOL, o PagSeguro (http://www.pagseguro.com.br). Também está disponível para download um servidor PagSeguro para testes. O servidor necessita do .Net Framework 2.0 para funcionar. ATENÇÃO Lembre-se de ajustar no web.config o encoding de seus requests e responses para ISO-8859-1 a fim de evitar problemas com caracteres especiais. </p>

<p> </p>

<p> 
<br/>... 
<br/> </p>

<p>PagSeguro TestServerAssista ao vídeo de exemplo de uso do servidor de testes PagSeguroServer </p>

<p>O PagSeguro TestServer é um servidor de testes, desenvolvido em .Net para que seja possível testar a integração de um sistema com o PagSeguro da Uol de forma offline em ambiente windows. </p>

<p>A] Como configurar o servidor PagSeguro:Instale o pacote do Servidor e inicie o &quot;PagSeguro TestServer&quot; Vá em Arquivo -&gt; Configurações e configure a URL da sua página de retorno automático Inicie o servidor através da barra de ferramentas ou em Arquivo -&gt; Servidor-&gt; Iniciar Seu servidor estará online escutando os seguintes endereços: URL de venda: http://localhost:9090/checkout/checkout.jhtml URL de Retorno Automático: http://localhost:9090/pagseguro-ws/checkout/NPI.jhtml B] Funcionamento:Ao receber uma venda, o servidor irá listá-la na tela principal. Selecione a venda e clique no ícone da lupa da barra de ferramentas para visualizar toda a venda. </p>

<p>Para disparar o retorno automático, selecione o Tipo de Pagamento, Status, insira o Valor do Frete no formato (0,00) e alguma anotação necessária e ao final clique em &quot;Alterar Status&quot;. Isto invocará a URL de retorno automático configurada passando as informações de retorno. </p>

<p>C] Como configurar os controles PagSeguro.Net para utilizar o servidor de testes:Para configurar o controle &quot;VendaPagSeguro&quot; Configure a propriedade &quot;UrlPagSeguro&quot; do controle: UrlPagSeguro = &quot;http://localhost:9090/checkout/checkout.jhtml&quot; 
<br/>Para configurar o controle &quot;RetornoPagSeguro&quot; Configure a propriedade &quot;UrlNPI&quot; do controle: UrlNPI = &quot;http://localhost:9090/pagseguro-ws/checkout/NPI.jhtml&quot;</p>

 title : The video-player-project Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Welcome to The Video Player Project!  This project makes use of the FLTK C++ library to create a simple &quot;video&quot; player. </p>

<p>IntroductionHello.  The Video Player Project is a work in progress created by students at the Florida Institute of Technology for an introductory C++ course, CSE 2050.  The goal of the project is to create a GUI interface using C++ and a library called FLTK.  We are to incorporate usual video player features to play a series of pictures one after another.     </p>

<p>NewsHow we&#39;re doing so far... </p>

<p>Tuesday, February 26, 2008:  </p>

<p>Google Code page created! Familiarized with code page and FLTK libraries First upload of video player code snippets. </p>

<p>Thursday, February 28, 2008: </p>

<p>Class hierarchy designed File chooser for opening multiple images created Box created and added to window to display the images </p>

<p>Friday, February 29, 2008: </p>

<p>Big changes to the project Added two new data structures to facilitate the video player The project now has separate objects for a list of images and a single image </p>

<p>Wednesday, March 5, 2008 </p>

<p>Still having a big problem with the FLTK libraries.  We are having trouble displaying an image on the screen because of some compilation flags Changed a good deal of the code around, cleaned up some commenting, and removed obsolete variables </p>

<p>Thursday, March 6, 2008 </p>

<p>We&#39;ve fixed the compilation problem with Dev-C++.  The project now compiles successfully without errors.  However, the program crashes immediately upon being run Changed the ImageFrame class to now support all types of images via the Fl_Shared_Image library </p>

<p>MAJOR UPDATE FOR MARCH 6, 2008The program is up and running once again.  Our code compiles and executes properly We have figured out how to attach and display an image in a box The ImageFrame class has been changed back to JPEG support only.  The documentation for Fl_Shared_Image was misinterpreted Friday, March 7, 2008 </p>

<p>Removed unnecessary includes and method calls from the files without images in them. Added more buttons and associated every button with a callback function. The callback functions work, they just need to be actually coded. Removed old reference code that was no longer needed. Centered the buttons on the window. Changed small bit of code that will probably prevent problems in the future. Added getCurrentFrame() method to FrameList. </p>

<p>Saturday, March 8, 2008 </p>

<p>Coded all of the functions for the buttons. Buttons should work as soon as we get the pictures to load. </p>

<p>Wednesday, March 12, 2008 </p>

<p>Changed everything back to Fl::repeat_timeout() </p>

<p>Thursday, March 13, 2008 </p>

<p>Changed everything possible to strings. Changed storage method so that instead of storing all of the images, it now stores their locations. Image is created when getImage() is called. </p>

<p>Sunday, March 16, 2008 </p>

<p>The video player portion of the project has been completed at revision 107 The player is capable of handling BMP images The program successfully loads up a series of images and plays back at 30 FPS All buttons work as intended Work will now begin on minor debugging and the second part of the project </p>

<p>Tuesday, March 18, 2008 </p>

<p>Second part of the project begins! The video player will now be used for detection of objects in motion Project details can be found in PDF format here </p>

<p>Saturday, March 22, 2008 </p>

<p>Added CustomImage.h to the project The header file is used in motion detection </p>

<p>Tuesday, April 1, 2008 </p>

<p>The project works as intended The video sequence can be shown in grayscale or with only moving objects Work will now begin on creating a box around moving objects </p>

<p>Tuesday, April 22, 2008 It&#39;s been a while since an update has been posted... </p>

<p>The player and all functions now work correctly The video player can play normally, grayscale, show difference, label images, and box moving images Hooray </p>

<p>Downloadv1.0Source Code Debian package How to installDebian packageDownload the lastest Debian package form Download section. Open a terminal. Go to the directory where you download the package. Excecute: dpkg -i video-tube-X.X_all.deb where X.X is the version of your package. Finish! Source CodeDownload the lastest Source package form Download section. Open a terminal. Go to the directory where you download the package. Excecute: tar xvf video-tube-X.X.tar.gz where X.X is the version of your package Install the dependencies: Python sudo aptitude install python. PyQt sudo aptitude install python-qt3. Beautiful Soup sudo aptitude install python-beautifulsoup. Excecute python main.py. Finish! WindowsDownload the lastest Source package form Download section. Go to the directory where you download the package. Untar this with your favourite program. Install the dependencies: Python. Beautiful Soup. PyQt. Excecute python main.py or double click on this. Finish!</p>

 title : The fit4data Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>AboutFIT4Data is a testing framework for data management applications built on the Java implementation of FIT.  It allows developers to write FIT-like tests using the programming language of their choice.  This is essential in the ETL domain where the key technical skills are UNIX scripting and the ETL language used on the project and most developers do not know Java (or any other OO language) so they cannot be expected to write fixtures in the usual fashion.   </p>

<p>For example, if you are an Ab Initio developer, you can use FIT4Data to specify input data sets and tests to run against the system under test using some slightly modified FIT fixtures and connectors provided as part of this project using FIT4Data&#39;s command line interface. </p>

<p>You test results will be written in an easy to read HTML format like this... </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Furthermore, FIT4Data provides direct support for common ETL tasks like integrating with a UNIX shell environment and maintaining reusable data sets.  The focus of the project is to further expand this capability to make it quicker and easier to write and run tests. </p>

<p>Licences, Libraries and AcknowledgementsFIT4Data is released under the GNU General Public License v3 and it uses other open source products as follows </p>

<p>FIT v1.1 (http://fit.c2.com) H2 Database (http://www.h2database.com/html/main.html) This product includes software developed by the Apache Software Foundation (http://www.apache.org/)... </p>

 title : The inbbplus2 Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The notion of contracts as interfaces annotated with preconditions,postconditions and invariants , is simple and practical. The interface defines everything the clients need to know, but no more than that. This Project focus is on developing a library of Desing by Contract for Java. JavaDbC uses Java 5 annotations, to define assertions based on AOP(http://www.eclipse.org/aspectj/) and OGNL(http://www.ognl.org/). </p>

<p>Quick start with Design by Contract in Java (Comming soon!)   </p>

<p>You can see the code and examples here: http://javadbc.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ </p>

<p>Example </p>

<p>package org.dbc.examples.genericstack;</p>

<p>import org.javadbc.attributes.DBC;
<br/>import org.javadbc.attributes.Ensure;
<br/>import org.javadbc.attributes.Invariant;
<br/>import org.javadbc.attributes.Require;</p>

<p>@DBC
<br/>@Invariant(&quot;getCount() &gt;= 0&quot;)
<br/>public interface IStack {
<br/>	
<br/>	/**
<br/>	 * Cantidad de items que contiene actualmente el Stack
<br/>	 * 
<br/>	 * @return
<br/>	 */
<br/>	int getCount();</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Retorna el item que esta en el tope de la pila
<br/>	 * 
<br/>	 * @return
<br/>	 */
<br/>	@Require(&quot;getCount() &gt; 0&quot;)
<br/>	public E getItem();</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Determina si el Stack esta vacio
<br/>	 * 
<br/>	 * @return
<br/>	 */
<br/>	@Ensure(&quot;{result}==(getCount()==0)&quot;)
<br/>	public boolean isEmpty();</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Cada nuevo Stack se inicializa en vacio o para re-inicializar una Stack
<br/>	 * existente
<br/>	 */
<br/>	void initialize();</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Pone un item g sobre el tope del Stack
<br/>	 * 
<br/>	 * @param g
<br/>	 */
<br/>	@Ensure(&quot;#arg0.equals(getItem()) &amp;&amp; ( getCount() == {old getCount()} + 1)&quot;)
<br/>	void put(E g);</p>

<p>	/**
<br/>	 * Saca el elemento que esta en el tope del Stack
<br/>	 * 
<br/>	 * @return
<br/>	 */
<br/>	@Require(&quot;getCount() &gt; 0 &quot;)
<br/>	@Ensure(&quot;getCount() == {old getCount()} - 1 &quot;)
<br/>	void remove();</p>

<p>}</p>

 title : The ringide Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Ring IDE, described as an Open Source pluggable, multiplatform and stable integrated development environment has the main goal of integrating a set of tools to make easier developing games in Fenix. One of the main goals that distingish this from other IDEs is that Ring IDE will focus mainly in supporting as many fenix file formats as possible, delegating to a second place the code editor. The reason for that is that one can write code more or less confortable in any code editor but there are no similar tools for Fenix file formats. Ring Ide is built under the phylosophy of “One IDE to rule them all”, an idea partially taken from the project Flamebird (another Open Source project for creating a Fenix IDE in which I participated) </p>

<p>And what about fenixlib? fenixlib is a class library (writen in Java) whose aim is to support Fenix File formats in java in an easy way. With these library, any Java programmer can manipulate easily Map, Fbm, Fpl, etc. files. The purpose is to encourage Fenix users with Java knoweldedges to write its own GUI tools as well as providing a separated library to be used in Ring IDE. </p>

<p>Currently the project is in an alpha state: fenixlib is completed for about a 35% (Map, Fpl, Pal, and Fbm support is included) and the Ring IDE is still in an envision phase. Ring IDE development will not start until fenixlib is in a mature state - say 70% - however, simple (but helpful) tools are being developed at the same time as the fenixlib.</p>

 title : The rubbish-ide Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The scion-lib Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A wrapper around the GHC API to provide IDE functionality. </p>

<p>For a variety of reasons there is no standard IDE for Haskell programmers.  Many Haskell programmers use Vim or Emacs, but many others use Visual Studio, Eclipse, Yi or various other editors.  There are efforts to provide IDE functionality for each of these platforms, leading to large duplication of efforts.  Maintaining each of these libraries is not feasible or negates the addition of new features. </p>

<p>Scion (rhymes with &quot;lion&quot;) is an IDE library, i.e., it does not provide a user interface, but rather an API for IDEs.  Scion provides: </p>

<p>A Haskell library that is higher-level than the GHC API (and can be changed independently of the GHC API.)  Furthermore, it aims to abstract over changes in the GHC API (wherever reasonably possible.) For frontends not written in Haskell, Scion provides a server that exposes as much of the Haskell API as possible.  The server uses JSON as the wire protocol since it is simple and libraries are available for a very wide range of systems. The goal is that new IDE features are added to Scion once and frontends need just implement the front-end specific code, thus minimising the amount of work for IDE maintainers. </p>

<p>Scion&#39;s main repository is hosted on Github.  If you have a Github account just click the &quot;fork&quot; button.  Otherwise you can get a copy via: </p>

<p>git clone git://github.com/nominolo/scion.gitFeaturesOpen and load a Cabal project (returning error messages) Background-typecheck file (returning error messages) Print type of (local) identifier at point Emacs FrontendHighlights error messages directly in the source, together with a tooltip Optional on-the-fly typechecking (idle-time based, or whenever file is saved) Completion on LANGUAGE names, pragmas, external module names and OPTIONS-flags Planned FeaturesGHCi REPL with all the modules from the current package available Many more ContributingIf you forked the project on Github, send a pull request.  Otherwise send a patch to the mailing list.</p>

 title : The Sibilla Test Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Short description:In a nutshell Sibilla aims at changing the point of view regarding test classes and classes under test. What we get is the focus being moved to the classes under test; from those classes, which of course are the most important ones of your projects, we obtain links to your test classes and test methods. In other words we define the classes and methods&#39; contract using tests, while also keeping track of tests that need to be run when a class/method under test has been modified. This is possible by collecting metadata sets that represent links between classes under test and test classes (and eventually more fine grained links between methods) and using them for a lot of purposes. Metadata can be collected from different sources: annotations on classes under test, instrument</p>

 title : The blackhat-toolkit Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Libraries for constructing, parsing, manipulating and serializing OAI-ORE Resource Maps. </p>

<p>Foresite is a JISC funded project which aims to produce a  demonstrator and test of the OAI-ORE standard by creating Resource Maps  of journals and their contents held in JSTOR, and delivering them as  ATOM documents via the SWORD interface to DSpace.  DSpace will  ingest these resource maps, and convert them into repository items which  reference content which continues to reside in JSTOR.  The Python  library is being used to generate the resource maps from JSTOR and the  Java library is being used to provide all the ingest, transformation and  dissemination support required in DSpace. </p>

<p>Both libraries support parsing and serialising in: ATOM, RDF/XML, N3,  N-Triples, Turtle and RDFa.</p>

<p>Python XMP Toolkit is wrapping Exempi  (using ctypes), a C/C++ XMP library based on Adobe XMP Toolkit, ensuring that future updates to the XMP standard are easily incorporated into the library with a minimum amount of work. </p>

<p>Python XMP Toolkit has been developed by: </p>

<p>ESA/Hubble - European Space Agency ESO - European Southern Observatory CRS4 - Centre for Advanced Studies, Research and Development in Sardinia </p>

<p>Support for parsing, manipulating, and serializing XMP data. Support for locating the XMP in a file, adding XMP to a file, or updating the XMP in a file. Support for nearly any file format with smart file handlers for JPEG, TIFF, GIF, PNG, PSD, InDesign, MOV, MP3, MPEG2, MPEG4, AVI, FLV, SWF, ASF, PostScript, P2, SonyHDV, AVCHD, UCF, WAV, XDCAM, XDCAMEX. An API very similar to Adobe XMP Toolkit, as well as more Pythonic methods as well. Based on Exempi 2.1.1 and Adobe XMP Toolkit 4.4.2 DocumentationSee http://www.spacetelescope.org/projects/python-xmp-toolkit/docs/index.html</p>

<p>AudioBlank Marshall MG15-CD graphically simulates Guitar amplifier Marshall MG 15 CD. It does not process the audio in any way. But it&#39;s useful for keeping the amp configuration while miking the amp.  </p>

<p>We tweak the knobs and switches in the actual amp (EQ, Volumes, Overdrive/Clean, FDD on/off etc.) to get the desired the sound  and mic the amp. If we want to continue the same recording later, we have to recreate the same settings in the amp. Otherwise we can not achieve the same tone. </p>

<p>Once you are happy with your tone in the amp, before hitting record </p>

<p>Insert AudiobBlank Marshall MG15-CD in the track Tweak the plugin so that it reflects your actual settings in the amp.  Hit record </p>

<p>Your host will save the settings along with the plugin. Later if you wish to continue the same track, fire up the plugin from the track, set your amp according to the plugin.</p>

 title : The bluez-pulseaudio Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Pulseaudio is a networked sound server, for both POSIX and Win32 systems. It acts like a proxy for sound applications. With it is possible to do software mixing of different audio streams (even if they are on different machines), transfer an audio stream between different machines over the network, change the sample format or channel count, among other things. </p>

<p>The benefit of integrating the Bluetooth Audio service into pulseaudio is that will be possible to make connections between the bluetooth audio streams and other audio streams on the computer. In example, it would be possible to have two people, each one with one bluetooth headset (or one bluetooth and one wired headset), talking on the same record channel of a VoIP application, mixing the two audio streams coming from the headsets into one that goes into the VoIP application. </p>

<p>In addition, would be also possible to have pulseAudio to control your bluetooth audio streams, lowering the volume of your (bluetooth or not) speakers and activating your headset when you receive a call on your VoIP system.</p>
 summary : <p>The program is an audio extractor and encoder: it interfaces with the DVD device, reads from a DVD Video, and allows the user to extract any audio track from any title/chapter, and encode it in wave, mp3 or ogg. </p>

 summary : <p>an easy mp3 based on atmega8 and vs1003b </p>

<p>avr mega8l mcu based ,c languague  source codes here for downloading and also the pcb board original protel type documents for pcb making.   随着数码技术在生活中的广泛应用，各种消费电子产品之间的数据交换变得非常频繁，而家庭音响也逐渐脱离磁带，CD,VCD等传统介质，而代之以存储卡，U盘，硬盘或网络硬盘。基于成本和内容更新方便与否的考虑，来设计一款以SD卡为介质的MP3音响。 本论文主要是设计一款具有优秀音质且成本低廉的音响音源，文件采用mp3格式，考虑到此种网络音乐格式的普遍性。SD卡读取方式为spi模式，充分利用单片机支持的总线结构，MP3解码技术，fat文件系统，实现完整的mp3的播放。 电路架构采用atmel公司的8位单片机atmega8L作为主控芯片，与vlsi公司的解码芯片vs1003b，将sd卡内的mp3文件解码输出为音频信号，通过音响输出。经实做结果显示此架构确能提供低失真度，低功耗的音质。 若加入性能更优秀的功放模块提高其输出功率，此产品可以改造成家庭hifi音响的一部分，或者加入无线RF传输功能，则可以实现无线音响的功能，使得在屋内各处都可收听到音乐，可应用于无线数字广播系统。</p>

 title : The raopd Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>raopd is (or more correctly, will be) software to stream audio from a Linux box to an Apple AirPort Express.  The system consists of two pieces.  The first piece is an ALSA kernel driver to provide an audio device for applications to use for audio output.  The second piece is a simple Linux daemon that packages up the stream, encrypts it, and transmits it over the network using the RAOP protocol. </p>

<p>raopd differs from raop_play and JustePort, two other RAOP implementations, in that raopd is not a music player, nor does it have a user interface--it is in many ways a simplified version of raop_play.  It is a kernel module and system daemon.  Audio applications see it as a hardware sound card, and it transmits the audio stream it receives unmodified to the AEX.   </p>

<p>One other significant change, not technical, is that raopd is a pure GPLv3 implementation.  All the code has been written by us, and it depends only on OpenSSL, with an appropriate license exception under the GPLv3 to permit linking against OpenSSL. </p>

<p>One other goal of this project is to create a software package that &quot;just works&quot;.  The module will load and the daemon will be started on boot via an init script, remaining idle until audio data is present, and returning to idle and releasing control of the AirPort when the audio stream ends. </p>

<p>The code is net yet fully functional.  If you&#39;ve arrived here looking for working software, please check back in a month or so.  While the core code works, and we&#39;re able to stream audio to the AirPort, much of the supporting code still remains to be written, and installation is a purely manual process.  Unless you&#39;re a C programmer, there isn&#39;t going to be anything useful or interesting here (and even then, it&#39;s probably not that interesting!)  If you want something that works now, try http://raop-play.sourceforge.net/ or http://nanocr.eu/software/justeport/</p>
 summary : <p>Raymond is a cross-platform DAISY Audio DTB Player supporting the Daisy 2.02 and ANSI/NISO Z3986-2005 DTB formats. </p>

 title : The soundsright Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Spectro-Edit reads in regular PCM audio files (currently, only 16-bit mono WAV is supported), then shows you the audio visually in a time vs. frequency plot. </p>

<p>The fun part is, you can &quot;paint out&quot; any part of the visualization and play back the audio subject to your modifications. When you are happy with the result, you can save your work back to a WAV file. </p>

<p>This could be useful for podcasting (edit out microphone noise, chair squeaks, phones ringing, and other background noise), music (make strange and unusual modifications to the sound for artistic reasons), research (visualize animal calls or noise pollution from nearby industrial activity), and general purpose geekery (which is why I made it). </p>

<p>To help get you started, check out the BasicInstructions and UsageExamples. </p>

<p>Enjoy! </p>

<p>Special ThanksThanks to Piotr Wendykier of Emory University for his JTransforms library, which Spectro-Edit uses for its fast and accurate DCT and IDCT routines. JTransforms is available under a MPL 1.1/GPL 2.0/ LGPL 2.1 tri-license. Spectro-Edit uses it under the terms of LGPL 2.1. </p>

<p>Thanks also to Mark James for his Silk icon set. Spectro-Edit uses a mix of original and butchered (by me) icons from this set. The Silk icons are available under the Creative Commons Attribution License 2.5 </p>

<p>Screenshot</p>

 title : The biopythongui Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is a GUI front-end for the BioPython module. BioPython is a module for python that contains tool for bioinformatics researchers. One problem with BioPython is that in order to use it in a powerful way one must be a python developer. This will change this. This will be designed basically to retrieve biological sequences (DNA, RNA, proteins) from online databases, such as NCBI, and bring those sequences into an environment where it is easy to manipulate them. Also, This will interface to BLAST and MEME so that researchers can use these tools as well, integrated with the database lookups. There will be many other features as well such as translating/transcribing DNA, RNA, and protein, visualizing the different sequences, modeling and genetic algorithm support, integrated command line for directly using python to manipulate sequences, and scripting. This will have most, if not all, of the features BioPython has, only instead of a messy code-driven interface, it will be graphical.</p>

 title : The captor Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Captor-AO ProjectA Software Product Line (SPL) consists of a set of software systems that share common features and fulfill the specific requirements of a particular domain. In order to make the products instantiation process faster and less prone to errors, the project of a SPL can adopt the utilization of application generators, which can automatically generate the SPL artifacts based on the specification of the variabilities of a particular product. Additionally, it can be noticed that certain crosscutting features of a product line have potencial to be reused in different domains, so they can be implemented using aspect oriented programming (AOP). </p>

<p>In this work, a process is proposed for the development of SPLs and automatic generation of products, considering the crosscutting concerns present in each application domain. The crosscutting concerns are related to the common features that are scattered around program divisions or modules of different domains. The process proposed here has the goal of enhancing the reuse of SPL features using AOP, allowing the design of SPL in a more cohesive way and, thus, easing its maintenance and evolution. Aiming at decreasing the effort needed to instantiate products from these SPL, this work also presents an extension to the Captor application generator, named Captor-AO.  </p>

<p>This generator supports the proposed process, allowing the creation of products composed  by features of different domains. Finally, a case study is presented in which Captor-AO is configured with two domains: a crosscutting domain for the persistence concern and a base domain compatible with this crosscutting domain, such that the generation of products can be done by composing features of both domains.</p>
 summary : <p>Still to come..., </p>

 title : The checkstyle-idea Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>DescriptionThis is a CheckStyle plug-in for JetBrain&#39;s IntelliJ IDEA. </p>

<p>At present this plugin is only having high priority fixes applied - if you have the time and inclination to continue feature development please drop me a line. </p>

<p>Unlike JetStyle, this plug-in was original written to provide real-time integration, in a similar manner to Eclipse-CS. From version 0.4 it also provides on-demand scanning for the current file and project. </p>

<p>UsageReal-time scanning is provided as an Inspection. On-demand scanning is available as a tab at (by default) the bottom of the IDEA window. </p>

<p>Configuration for both the inspection and the on-demand scanning is done via the CheckStyle item in the Settings panel. </p>

<p>Click on Real-time Scan and you will be able to specify the report severity and activate the inspection as appropriate. </p>

<p>Current FeaturesIn version 3.x:    </p>

<p>CheckStyle 5.0 support. Per-module configuration. </p>

<p>In version 2.x: </p>

<p>Scan files in real-time with an IDEA inspection. Scan the current file, module or project on demand. Standard Java rules are built in, or specify your own CheckStyle file. Ability to add third party checks to the classpath. Ability to define external properties. Version 1.x is for IDEA6. 2.x is for IDEA 7 and (from 2.2) 8. Both of these support CheckStyle 4 and are no longer maintained. </p>

<p>Version 3 support CheckStyle 5 only, and from 3.0.5 is compatible with IDEA 9. </p>

<p>Current LimitationsThe plugin will throw exceptions if used with class files targeted at a later version than that of the JDK used by IDEA. In particular, this will affect Mac users with the pre-release of JDK6. The solution is to target class files at the version of the IDEA JRE (i.e. 1.5 for Mac users). Thanks to J. G. Christopher. If you change the configuration options the real-time scan will not be updated until the file is either changed or reopened. We do not check if a property definition is required for a given file. Hence you can exit configuration without setting required properties. Given, however, that CheckStyle files can change without the plug-in being aware this is something we&#39;ll always have to live with to some degree. CheckStyle errors and warnings from the inspection are both shown at a single level, as IDEA will only allow one warning level for an inspection.</p>

 summary : <p>DevJFX is a collection of examples and code snippets that demonstrate the capabilities of the JavaFX Script language.  </p>

<p>JavaFX Script is a statically typed, declarative scripting language from Sun Microsystems that runs in the web browser, on the desktop and on the cell phone. It is focused on enabling developers and designers to quickly create compelling 2D and 3D user interfaces without having to be experts in graphics libraries. It borrows idioms from SVG, functional languages and Java. It&#39;s tightly integrated with Java such that an application&#39;s UI can be written in JavaFX Script while the heavy lifting can still be done in Java. </p>

<p>In many ways JavaFX Script competes with Adobe Flash and Microsoft Silverlight. </p>

<p>Related web site: DevJFX.com</p>
