 summary : <p>Aims and ObjectivesS5 (A Simple Standards-Based Slide Show System) is an entirely browser based slide show system built on web standards such as XHTML, CSS and JavaScript. S5 is rudimentary as a slide show system compared to other slide show systems such as Google Presentations. </p>

<p>This project will build on S5’s current limitations as we web-based slide show system. Also this project will explore ways in which S5 can make better use of the collaborative possibilities of Web 2.0, such as social-networking sites, wikis and blogs. This will involve documenting and evaluating the existing code base of several slide show systems and then gathering customer requirements for enhancements. </p>

<p>The key objective of the project will be to design and develop a web-based slide show system that incorporates a number of Web 2.0 technologies, and in essence compete against Microsoft PowerPoint and Google Presentations. An Extreme Programming (XP) approach will be adopted since this project will emphasise on customer involvement, teamwork and creating prototypes in quick succession. A team of developers will implement the proposed enhancements entirely on XHTML, CSS and JavaScript. </p>

 title : The equaked Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Using data obtained via accelerometer readings on time-synchronized, collective E-puck robots, we propose a framework to detect in real-time the geographic epicenter of a radially-emitted shock wave. Combining techniques to obtain swarm synchronization, centralized communication and the parameters for   mathematical   multilateration,   our   research   provides foundational work for more advanced detection and localization of earthquake-like vibrations in swarm-intelligent systems. With an experimental setup consisting of three immobile E-puck robots,   our   methodology   has   shown   potential   to   provide accurate geographic localization of simple shock waves in a two-dimensional triangular arena. Unfortunately, due to hardware limitations   on   the   E-puck   robot   accelerometers,   actual experimental results were unattainable. This project highlights and contextualizes our implementation and outlines the crux of the problem in order to motivate future related research.</p>

<p>Supporting ETL ProjectsThis is where we host the documents that are intended to aid members of ETL start, run, and contribute to projects.  ETL is an umbrella group that strives to give developers/researchers the support they need so that they can focus their energy and time on development rather than administration. We also aim to provide an active and engaging environment, both online and in person, to aid in education, project and personal interaction, and introduction to new technologies and ideas. </p>

<p>We believe strongly that transparency will make us a better organization It adds a democratic aspect to ETL. Any member or outside interested party can make suggestions and corrections. If everything is open and up for discussion than nothing is permanent. This will help ETL adapt to new situations and tools and more easily overcome problems. The work we are doing to create a robust development cooperative can help others. Anyone is welcome to view, use, and adapt our structure to fit their needs.</p>

 title : The haga Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>HagaHaga is a presentation support tool for UNIX. If you have your presentation in PDF, you can use Haga to add auxiliary notes to individual slides and setup the intended length of your presentation. Then in most cases you can just press the fullscreen button and the presentation is running. Haga automagically detects if the computer has multiple screens attached. If it does, Haga will show its full user interface to you and the audience will see only the slides.  </p>

<p>It is of course work in progress. The current version is usable, but the user interface has many quirks that need to be sorted out. It depends on the GTK and Glade libraries for user interface, Poppler for rendering PDF and zlib for storing data. This means it should be compilable under many UNIX systems and possibly in a distant future under Windows too. </p>

<p>Installation is simple. Just download the source archive, unpack it and do the usual: </p>

<p>./configure
<br/>make
<br/>make installObligatory screenshot:</p>

 title : The lecture-maker Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Lecture MakerAn application to make a lecture out of a presentation and a video </p>

<p>Usagepython lecture_maker.py config_file contains the information about the process, and should be ini format. Each file to be created should have its own top-level section, with a familiar name as the section name. </p>

<p>Each section should have the following config options: </p>

<p>Name  Description  Required or Default   presentation_file  The filename of the presentation to import     presentation_timings  The timings for the slide changes. Comma separated list of integers (seconds)     video_file  The video filename to import     output_file  The output file name     output_framerate  The output frame rate  default=10   output_size  the size in pixels of the output video WxH  default=640x240   output_presentation_size  The size of the presentation in the output file  default=320x240   output_presentation_position  The position of the presentation in the output file relative to the top-left  default=0x0   output_presentation_ontop  Whether the presentation will appear over the video in the output  default=yes   output_video_size  The size of the video in the output file  default=320x240   output_video_position  The position of the video in the output file  default=0x320  </p>

<p>An example: </p>

<p>[MyVideo]
<br/>presentation_file = formatted_ppt/1.odp
<br/>presentation_timings = 0, 5, 10, 15, 20, 25, 30, 35, 40
<br/>video_file = vids/1.mpg
<br/>output_framerate = 25
<br/>output_file = out/1.avi
<br/>output_size = 720x576
<br/>output_video_size = 720x576
<br/>output_video_position = 0x0
<br/>output_presentation_size = 160x120
<br/>output_presentation_position = 50x50
<br/>output_presentation_ontop = yes</p>

<p>= Requirements =</p>

<p>== Linux ==
<br/>  * Python &gt;= 2.4
<br/>  * FFMpeg (compiled with the things you need)
<br/>  * PIL - Python Imaging Library
<br/>  * Openoffice with Python UNO Bindings</p>

<p>== Windows ==
<br/>  * Python &gt;= 2.4
<br/>  * PIL - Python Imaging Library
<br/>  * Powerpoint
<br/>  * Python win32com bindings</p>

 title : The py2llvm Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>py2llvm is an another approach translating codes in Python syntax into LLVM IR for fast execution. </p>

<p>You can develop &amp; run your code in Python for rapid-prototyping phase. Once your code become in stable, your code is turned into native code by py2llvm and it runs extremely fast(as fast as C). </p>

<p>py2llvm enables easy development of your performance-oriented algorithm while its code runs as fast as C. </p>

<p>Since Python is a dynamic programming language, not all feature of Python can be mapped into LLVM IR by py2llvm. Only statically type-inferable and no object-oriented code fragment could be translated, but this is almost enough for performance-oriented programs for example numerical computation and graphics. </p>

<p>Here is a example translation by py2llvm. </p>

<p>def muda():</p>

<p>    a = 1
<br/>    b = 2</p>

<p>    c = a + b-&gt; </p>

<p>define void @muda() {
<br/>entry:
<br/>	%tmp0 = alloca i32		;  [#uses=2]
<br/>	store i32 1, i32* %tmp0
<br/>	%tmp1 = load i32* %tmp0		;  [#uses=1]
<br/>	%a = alloca i32		;  [#uses=2]
<br/>	store i32 %tmp1, i32* %a
<br/>	%tmp2 = alloca i32		;  [#uses=2]
<br/>	store i32 2, i32* %tmp2
<br/>	%tmp3 = load i32* %tmp2		;  [#uses=1]
<br/>	%b = alloca i32		;  [#uses=2]
<br/>	store i32 %tmp3, i32* %b
<br/>	%tmp4 = load i32* %a		;  [#uses=1]
<br/>	%tmp5 = load i32* %b		;  [#uses=1]
<br/>	%tmp6 = add i32 %tmp4, %tmp5		;  [#uses=1]
<br/>	%c = alloca i32		;  [#uses=1]
<br/>	store i32 %tmp6, i32* %c</p>

<p>return:
<br/>	ret void
<br/>}# SIMD code
<br/>from MUDA import *</p>

<p>def test(a = vec, b = vec):</p>

<p>    return a + b-&gt; </p>

<p>define  @test( %a,  %b) {
<br/>entry:
<br/>	%tmp4 = alloca 		;  [#uses=2]
<br/>	store  %a, * %tmp4
<br/>	%tmp5 = alloca 		;  [#uses=2]
<br/>	store  %b, * %tmp5
<br/>	%tmp6 = load * %tmp4		; &lt;&gt; [#uses=1]
<br/>	%tmp7 = load * %tmp5		; &lt;&gt; [#uses=1]
<br/>	%tmp8 = add  %tmp6, %tmp7		; &lt;&gt; [#uses=1]
<br/>	ret  %tmp8
<br/>}</p>

 summary : <p>This project is Free. I&#39;ve created it for my own usage but I thought I&#39;d serve for other projects. Developing softwares for free, without meeting the users, needs a good communication between us. I&#39;d be infinitely grateful you send a little email at andematunum@gmail.com so that I know what&#39;s going on. If I have no feedback, I cannot improve, or correct the bugs. </p>

<p>SDL_Layer is a mechanism allowing the blitting of surfaces (sprites, animations, effects) on different planes/layers of the display. It is capable of doing scrolling with each layer having its own scrolling factor, to create depth effects. It is build on top of SDL (http://www.libsdl.org). </p>

<p>It is useful for example in a game, when one wants to have a background image, obstacles, and a foreground effect (clouds, fog, rain, etc.) </p>

<p>This library takes care of all the refresh problems when using a &quot;dirty rectangles&quot; method, reblitting notably the specific zones of each layer. You can also choose a &quot;whole refresh&quot; method using SDL_Flip. </p>

<p>Take a glance at the WiKi and see what it will be capable of. </p>

<p>Here is a screenshot from the scroll demo:  </p>

<p>In this demo, the display is made of 3 separate layers: </p>

<p>The canyon background The &quot;DEMO&quot; text The cloud layer What is Andematunum ? An amazing medieval town in the countryside of france with fortifications: http://www.tourisme-langres.com/</p>

 title : The semanticfm Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Serveur web sémantique pour Last.fm</p>

<p>Nom  Contact   Maximilien Perrin    Camille Roux  Website  </p>

<p>ObjectifL’objectif de notre projet est d’exploiter des données extraites de Last.FM grâce à son API pour fournir une navigation directe et intuitive parmi les artistes et styles de musiques. L’utilisateur peut ainsi découvrir de nouveaux artistes et des morceaux de musique originaux suivant ses goûts musicaux, et obtenir des informations sur ce qu’il souhaite.  </p>

<p>Notre projet comporte deux parties fondamentales. La première partie consiste à développer un utilitaire destiné à récupérer un ensemble d’informations à partir des services web d’AudioScrobbler, afin de constituer une base sémantique représentative des musiques existantes. L’API mise à disposition ne permet pas de récupérer les  données de façon globale, mais seulement de façon ponctuelle : on peut par exemple récupérer à partir d’un artiste précis ses artistes proches, ses tags, ses albums... mais pas l’ensemble des artistes existants. Nous avons donc décidé d’utiliser un parcours en largeur sur le graphe des artistes proches afin de constituer une liste d’artistes, puis  pour chaque récupérer ses tags et ses albums. Cette méthode permet de constituer rapidement une base de  connaissances à partir d’un nom d’artiste. </p>

<p>La seconde partie de notre projet consiste en un site web permettant l’accès et la navigation parmi les données récupérées. Ce site, basé sur le moteur sémantique Sewese, devait respecter un certain nombre de contraintes que nous nous étions fixées. Tout d&#39;abord, nous souhaitions que le site soit ergonomique afin qu&#39;il puisse être  ludique pour l&#39;utilisateur. Nous tenions également à respecter certaines normes d&#39;accessibilité afin que le site puisse être utilisé par des déficients visuels ainsi que pour favoriser le référencement par les moteurs de recherche. </p>

<p>Scénarios d’utilisationComme nous l&#39;avons dit précédemment, nous avons décidé de faire en sorte que le site puisse offrir la possibilité à l&#39;utilisateur de réaliser un voyage dans la musique. Nous voulions qu&#39;il puisse facilement naviguer entre les styles de musique et les artistes. </p>

<p>Pour cela, nous avons décidé d&#39;afficher un nuage de tags en première page représentant les tags les plus utilisés dans notre base. Un clic sur un tag permet d&#39;afficher la liste des artistes qui correspondent le plus au tag en question, avec la photo du groupe si elle est disponible. Enfin, un clic sur un artiste affiche la page de l&#39;artiste lui- même qui est divisée en trois parties : la liste de ses albums, un nuage des tags correspondant à l&#39;artiste et aussi, les artistes qui ont un style proche de celui de l&#39;artiste. </p>

<p>Il est à noter qu&#39;il est possible de revenir sur le nuage de tags du départ à tout moment en cliquant sur le logo du site. </p>

<p>Enfin, nous avons ajouté un champ de recherche dans la bannière qui permet à l&#39;utilisateur de faire une recherche parmi les tags et les artistes, ce qui lui permet d&#39;accéder rapidement à l&#39;information s&#39;il le souhaite.</p>
 title : The sibyl Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>An Android music player.This project has been started within the context of a school project. We are four students from a French enginering school of Lyon called INSA. Our aim is to create an application for the Android platform, the Google operating system for mobile phones.  </p>

<p>The application is a music player, almost like Amarok, Winamp, iTunes or whatever audio player you can find. It has basics functionnalities such as play modes / smart playlists / library management. There is also a cover manager which can download missing covers. Sibyl uses Android SDK possibilities such as animations and touch mode. </p>

<p>Further developments will maybe consider the interaction with social networks (last.fm for example). </p>

<p>Do not hesitate to mail us to suggest features or to report bugs. You can find us on #sibyl-dev on Freenode.</p>

 title : The splitshow Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>SplitShowA tool for the dual-head presentation of PDF slides on Mac OS X, most likely using a laptop and a projector. The project arose out of the need to correctly project slides created with LaTeX&#39;s BEAMER class. </p>

<p>Call for IconsAs you can see, SplitShow is still lacking a proper icon. Any contributions are more than welcome! We do have some ideas, we&#39;re just not very artistic. Email us for more information. And thanks in advance! </p>

<p>Screenshot </p>

<p>Dual-Head Full Screen Mode at Native ResolutionsTraditional PDF viewers require two displays to be in &quot;mirror&quot; mode in order to show the same image on both. The -- maybe not so obvious -- disadvantage of this is that the higher-resolution display is forced to used the resolution of the lower-resolution one. By keeping the two displays at their respective native resolutions in &quot;extended desktop&quot; mode, your slides will always look great on either side. </p>

<p>DonationsIf you think SplitShow saved your day, consider a donation to support our effort. Thanks in advance to all who donate! </p>

 title : The starscream-slideshow Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>GigaPan Stereo Imaging                                 </p>

<p>Project SummeryGigaPan is a system that consists of a robotic camera mount that uses a standard digital camera to capture a grid of pictures of a scene and custom software that stitches that grid together into a very high- resolution (gigapixel and up) panoramic image. Building off this technology, Stereo GigaPan (with backing from West Virginia University and NASA/Ames Intelligent Robotics Group) modifies the camera mount to support an additional consumer-grade digital camera. With two cameras the system now has the ability to ascertain depth information from a scene, which is used to create highly detailed 3D images and models. Combined with the addition of new remote control and robust power management systems, Stereo GigaPan greatly improves functionality while keeping costs within the budget of any aspiring photographer. </p>

<p>Navigation LinksProject Wiki (Information about the project, public documentation, tips and tricks) Group File Storage (sample images, private files, items that should not go into repository) CpE/CS 480 Class Group Website (Official Class Documentation Postings) Hardware Setup (using the new camera mounts) NOTE: Some of the links on this site are private links, and are not available to the public.</p>
